# Beastmen Compendium

In the shadowed depths of ancient forests, where sunlight scarcely penetrates the dense canopy, the beastmen gather as they prepare to make war on all of civilization. These vile humanoids are a grotesque blend of horned beast and man, embodying the primal savagery of the animal kingdom and the cunning malevolence of humanity. Their twisted forms are a mockery of the human shape, with gnarled horns, coarse fur, and bestial visages that inspire fear and revulsion.

The beastmen harbor a deep-seated loathing for civilization and its creations. They view the structured order of cities and towns as an affront to their wild and chaotic nature, and they take perverse pleasure in despoiling the works of more civilized races. This hatred is not just ideological but deeply instinctual, driving them to relentless acts of destruction and desecration.

Their abode is the untamed wilderness of the dark forests, a labyrinthine world of shadows and danger. The beastmen are not alone in these murky realms; they often form temporary alliances with other destructive monsters and malevolent entities that share their disdain for order and harmony. These dark alliances make the heart of the forests a place of nightmares, where few dare to tread.

\columnbreak

The society of the beastmen is characterized by rowdiness, impulsiveness, and a lack of any refined culture. They live for the thrill of the hunt, the joy of battle, and the ecstasy of indulgence in their base desires. Their communities are driven by a brutal hierarchy where strength and savagery are the only currencies of respect. Hedonism and bloodlust are not just common but celebrated, and their rituals and revels are debauched affairs that often end in violence or worse.

Despite their apparent lack of sophistication, the beastmen are not to be underestimated. They possess cunning and knowledge of their woodland domains, making them formidable adversaries. Their raids are swift and brutal, striking like a tempest and leaving behind only ruin and despair. In the savage wilds, the beastmen reign supreme, a constant reminder of the dark and wild forces that lurk just beyond the boundaries of the civilized world.

This document provides content to help you run games that heavily feature the beastmen or any of the savage creatures that dwell in their forest domain. This content ranges from new spells used by the beastmen to a bestiary of the different types of beastmen and the monsters they utilize. Whether the players only have a minor side quest featuring beastmen or an entire campaign, any of the content here can be used to enhance your games.

# Running Beastmen Adventures 

The setting you're running your adventures in will help determine the origin of the beastmen and how they fit into your world. They may be irredeemably evil monsters who serve dark gods and seek the downfall of civilization. They may have once been rowdy, uncouth humans who succumbed to their wild impulses and were cursed with bestial forms. Or, they may be a savage but misunderstood race of forest dwellers the players are able to reason with.

Regardless of their origins, there are some common traits that define the beastmen and the creatures they ally with:

* **Driven By Base Urges:** All humans experience primal drives that push them towards violence or hedonism and must be controlled through discipline and civility. Beastmen lack and actively despise such forces of restraint and wholly give themselves to their debauched urges. They are wild and undisciplined in combat and prone to extreme and destructive revelry whenever given the chance. This makes them aggressive and unpredictable enemies but also limits their ability to organize and build anything of value.

* **Loathing of Civilization:** Beastmen lack the ability to create any civilization's marvelous works, and in turn, they hate all such creations. The creations of civilization allow softer, weaker humanoids to hold them at bay, and as such, beastmen seek to tear down civilization in all its forms so the playing field can be tipped in their favor. While beastmen will readily plunder the works of civilization for their own use, they will never put any effort into maintaining anything they've taken.

* **Might Makes Right:** Beastmen society is as uncivilized as one could imagine, and status within their clans is generally determined by strength and intimidation (though some cunning beastmen can rise in power through other means). The leaders of beastmen control their forces using such means and must always be ready to put down challengers while trying to maintain some form of cohesion among their wild and rowdy kin.

\columnbreak

### Beastmen Motivations
Most beastmen have simple motivations driven by base impulses that rarely stretch far into the future. They seek to gratify their animalistic urges which tend to include violence and destruction. They also seek to rise in status among their clan whenever possible, asserting dominance over others whenever the opportunity presents itself.

Leaders among the beastmen may have longer-term goals that involve bringing about the downfall of towns, cities, or even whole kingdoms. They find ways to tactically channel the destructive capabilities of their tribe to maximum effect, allowing them to pursue larger and grander acts of destruction.

When role-playing beastmen, don't overthink them. They are usually at the mercy of their destructive impulses and will pursue whatever is most likely to bring them immediate gratification. However, they are not mindless, and many still possess a low cunning, allowing them to plot ways to achieve their goals. They also possess a strong sense of self-preservation, which is often at odds with their impulsive nature. Beastmen can very quickly flip from wild abandon to panicked cowardess.

#### Common Beastmen Motivations
* Destroy Edifice of Civilization (Town, City, Caravan, Etc.)
* Indulge in Violence or Hedonism
* Gain Status in Clan
* Exact Vengeance on Enemy
* Appease Primal Gods
* Secure Forest Territory

### Tactics of the Beastmen Forces
The combat tactics used by the different types of beastmen are described along with each individual creature's description later in this document. When beastmen forces come together to form large war herds, they are able to operate with a level of coordination that belies their savage and impulsive nature. Though they aren't known for their intelligence, beastmen can employ tactics that resemble a cross between those used by a pack of predatory beasts and a gang of malicious bullies. They can work together to bring down powerful targets but get malicious glee when mobbing vulnerable victims.

Beastmen prefer rapid surprise attacks, relying on wild, savage, bravado, and bloodlust to immediately put their foes on the back foot. So long as they are pressing their advantage, the beastmen can rely on savage aggression to compensate for their lack of organization. However, if the tables turn on them, the craven and undisciplined nature of the beastmen causes their fighting force to quickly begin losing cohesion as tactics fall apart and many begin to flee. Only a beastman force led by a powerful leader can maintain its integrity in the face of such adversity.

<br>

# New Spells

## Lore of Beasts
This brand of magic draws on the power of the wilds and the animals that inhabit them. Those who practice it avoid civilization and live hermitic lives in the savage and untamed wilderness. Their magic harnesses the power of the beasts they dwell alongside, often by summoning wild spirits or unleashing the inner savagery of themselves and others to transform them into primeval creatures. The following spells are examples of the types of magic users of the Lore of Beasts often wield.

#### Amber Spear

*3rd-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60 feet
- **Components:**  V S M (A Piece of Amber)
- **Duration:**  Instantaneous
- **Classes:**   Druid, Ranger
___

You conjure a large amber hunting spear and launch it in a straight line at a point you can see within range. Upon reaching its destination or striking a solid surface, the spear shatters, producing an explosion within a 10-foot-radius sphere centered on that point. The spear can pass through spaces occupied by creatures and objects of large size or smaller. Each creature the spear moves through, as well as those within the explosion's radius, must make a Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 6d6 piercing damage; on a successful one, the damage is halved.


***At Higher Levels.***  When casting this spell using a 4th-level spell slot or higher, the range increases by 20 feet and the damage by 1d6 for each slot level above 3rd.

\columnbreak

<br><br>


#### Aspect of the Beast

*4th-level  transmutation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 bonus action
- **Range:** Touch
- **Components:**  V, S
- **Duration:**  Concentration, Up to 1 hour.
- **Classes:**   Druid, Ranger
___

Upon touching a willing creature, you imbue it with bestial might. For the duration, the creature manifests a bestial weapon of your choice from the list below. When it takes the Attack action on its turn, it can make an additional attack with the bestial weapon as part of that action. The weapon is treated as a simple weapon with which the creature is proficient. Unless otherwise stated, it uses its Strength modifier for attack and damage rolls made with the weapon.

**Ripping Jaws.** The creature's mouth becomes filled with dagger-like teeth. Its jaws deal 2d8 piercing damage on a hit. If the bite damages a creature, the user gains temporary hit points equal to half the piercing damage dealt, which last until the spell ends.

**Tearing Claws.** The creature's hands transform into blade-like claws. These claws deal 2d6 slashing damage on a hit and count as finesse weapons. The creature can choose to replace any of its melee attacks made with the Attack action with its claws, including any off-hand attacks.

**Ramming Horns.** Gnarled horns grow from the creature's head. The horns deal 2d8 bludgeoning damage on a hit. If the creature moves at least 15 feet straight toward a target and then hits it with a horn attack, the attack deals an extra 2d8 bludgeoning damage, and if the target is Large or smaller, the creature can choose to push it up to 15 feet away.

 <img src='https://i.ibb.co/LN1X4rk/Shaman-of-Forgotten-Ways-Mt-G-Art-1024x750.png' style='position:absolute;right:-0px;top:-20px;width:820px;transform:scaleX(1)' />

#### Bestial Spirit

*4th-level conjuration*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 40 feet
- **Components:**  V
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**   Druid, Ranger
___

A Large spectral beast appears at a location you choose within range. Though it appears substantial, it is intangible and can be passed through and occupied by other creatures.

Any hostile creature within 5 feet of the beast is so distracted by its presence that it has disadvantage on attack rolls. At the end of each of your turns, each hostile creature within 5 feet of the beast must make a Dexterity saving throw as the beast assaults it. The creature takes 4d8 force damage on a failed save, or half as much on a successful save. 

If a hostile creature moves more than 5 feet away from the beast, that creature must make the same saving throw against the beast's damage effect unless it took the Disengage action.

At the start of each of your turns, if no hostile creatures are within 5 feet of the beast, it moves up to 40 feet toward the closest hostile creature it can see. The beast has blindsight out to 120 feet and is blind beyond this range.

***At Higher Levels.***  When casting this spell using a 5th-level spell slot or higher, the beast's damage increases by 1d4 for each slot level above 4th.



\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

> ##### New Condition: Quickened
> A quickened creature gains an additional action on each of its turns. That action can be used only to take the Attack (one weapon attack or unarmed strike only), Dash, Disengage, Hide, or Use an Object action. The *haste* spell applies the quickened condition among its other effects, and a creature cannot benefit from the quickened condition from multiple sources at once.


<br>

#### Call of the Pack

*5th-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 Bonus Action
- **Range:** 60 feet
- **Components:**  V
- **Duration:**  1 round
- **Classes:**   Ranger
___

Unleashing a primal howl, you stir the wild fervor within your allies. You and up to three other creatures you are aware of within range that can hear you are quickened* until the start of your next turn. While quickened this way, these creatures gain advantage on attack rolls against any enemy if at least one of their allies is within 5 feet of that enemy and the ally isn't incapacitated.

**New condition described above*

#### Impenetrable Pelt

*5th-level  transmutation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1  action
- **Range:** 60 feet
- **Components:**  V, S, M (a tuft of fur)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, Up to 1 hour
- **Classes:**   Druid, Ranger
___

You weave magic to sheathe a willing creature you can see within range in a layer of tough fur and hide. For the spell's duration, any bludgeoning, piercing, or slashing damage the target takes is reduced by 5. This reduction applies before any resistances.

***At Higher Levels.***  When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 6th level or higher, the damage reduction increases by 1 for each slot level above 5th.




 <img src='https://i.ibb.co/2cTRzC2/Spirit-of-the-Aldergard-Kaldheim-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute;right:-50px;top:-90px;width:1100px;transform:scaleX(1)' />

#### Monstrous Transformation

*6th-level transmutation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 bonus action
- **Range:** Self
- **Components:**  V
- **Duration:**  Until dispelled
- **Classes:**   Druid, Sorcerer, Warlock
___

Drawing from wild energies, you transform into a mighty primal form of your choice: a **Feral Manticore**, a **Ravenous Hydra**, or a **Savage Dragon**. While transformed, you adopt the stat block of the selected beast (found later in this document). Your game statistics, including mental ability scores, are replaced by those of the chosen form, but you maintain your alignment and personality.

While in this new form:
* You assume its hit points.
* Your spell attack modifier and spell save DC replace its attack modifiers and saving throw DCs.
* If you're reduced to 0 hit points, you make death saving throws as usual. If you die, you revert to your true form.
* You can't speak, cast spells, or undertake any action requiring hands or speech.
* Your gear melds into your new form, rendering it inaccessible. As such, you can't activate, wield, or benefit from any of your equipment.

To attempt to end the spell, you may use your action to make a DC 15 saving throw using your original form's spellcasting ability modifier. On a successful save, the spell ends. However, if you fail this save three or more times within 8 hours, you must complete a long rest before attempting to end the spell again. A remove curse spell will also end the transformation.

If you take a long or short rest in your new form, only your new form gains the benefits of the rest

***At Higher Levels.***  When cast using a spell slot of 7th level or higher, the new form gains an additional 25 hit points for each slot level above 6th. If cast using a 9th-level slot, any features the new form can use only once per day can now be used three times per day.

\columnbreak

#### Primal Dominance

*2nd-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 30 feet
- **Components:**  V, S
- **Duration:**  10 minutes
- **Classes:**   Bard, Druid, Ranger
___

You emanate a commanding presence, compelling a primal creature to submit. Choose a beast, monstrosity, giant, dragon, or fey within range that can see and hear you. If the creature's Intelligence is 8 or higher, the spell has no effect. Otherwise, it must make a Wisdom saving throw. On a failed save, it becomes charmed and frightened by you until the end of your next turn. Regardless of the save's outcome, you gain a +5 bonus to Charisma (Intimidation) and Wisdom (Animal Handling) checks when interacting with that creature until the spell concludes.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a 3rd-level spell slot or higher, you can target one additional creature for each slot level above 2nd.




#### Summon Flock

*1st-level conjuration*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** Self
- **Components:**  V, S, M (A worm or bug)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 hour
- **Classes:**   Druid, Ranger
___

Upon casting, you summon three crows that circle above you for the duration of the spell. As a bonus action, you can direct one of the crows to dive at a creature or object within 120 feet. Make a ranged spell attack against the target. On a hit, it takes 2d4 piercing damage. If the attack is a critical hit, the target is blinded until the start of your next turn. Regardless of the outcome, the directed crow is expended. The spell ends if all crows are expended. For each crow circling above you, you gain a +1 bonus to Wisdom (Perception) checks.


***At Higher Levels.***  When you cast this spell using a 2nd-level spell slot or higher, you summon an additional crow for each slot level above 1st.

#### Wild Surge

*3rd-level transmutation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 30 feet
- **Components:**  V S M (a tuft of fur and a fang)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 10 minutes
- **Classes:**   Druid, Ranger
___

Select a willing creature within range to tap into its primal nature, transforming it into a bestial form. For the duration of the spell, the creature receives the following benefits:

<br>

* It gains 20 temporary hit points.
* It gains a +2 bonus to AC.
* It gains a +2 bonus to Strength saving throws and checks.
* It gains a +2 bonus to Wisdom (Perception) checks and Charisma (Intimidation) checks.
* When it hits with a melee weapon attack or unarmed strike, it deals one extra die of its damage.

***At Higher Levels.***  When casting this spell using a 4th-level spell slot or higher, the targeted creature gains an additional 5 temporary hit points for each slot level above 3rd.

> *Huge monstrosity, unaligned*

> - **Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 16
> - **Languages** You understand the languages you can speak in your normal form
> - **Challenge** 8 (3,900 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&ensp; **Proficiency Bonus** +3
> ___

> ***Tail Spikes.*** You have twelve tail spikes.
>
> ***Pounce.*** If you move at least 10 feet straight toward a creature and then hit it with a claw attack on the same turn, the target must succeed on a DC 16 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone.
> 
> <br><br>
> 
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** You make three attacks: one with your bite, one with your claws, and one with your tail spines. If both the claw and bite attacks hit the same target, the target is grappled (escape DC 16). Until this grapple ends, you can't use its bite or claw on another target.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +10 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 19 (2d12 + 6) piercing damage. If the target is prone, it takes 32 (4d12 + 6) piercing damage instead.
>
> ***Claw.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +10 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 17 (2d10 + 6) slashing damage.
>
> ***Tail Spike.*** *Ranged Weapon Attack:* +7 to hit, range 100/200 ft., one target. *Hit:* 15 (2d8 + 6) piercing damage plus 10 (3d6) poison damage.
>
> ***Toxic Volley.*** You fire six of your tail spikes at a point you can see within 100 feet. Each creature in a 15-foot-radius, 15-foot-high cylinder centered on that point must make a Dexterity saving throw against your spell save DC, taking 15 (2d8 + 6) piercing damage and 10 (3d6) poison damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one.
>
> ***Regrow Spikes (1/Day).*** You regrow all of your spent spikes.

## Lore of Death

This brand of magic plays on the nature of mortality and fragility of life, though it is strictly distinct from traditional necromancy, as it embraces the inevitability of death rather than attempting to deny it. Its users can manipulate negative energy, sap the vitality of foes, and instill mortal terror in those around them. The following spells are examples of the types of magic users of the Lore of Death often wield.

#### Aspect of Dread
*2nd-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A white feather)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Bard, Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard 
___

You envelop a creature you can see within range in a terrifying aura. Every other creature within 10 feet of the target must make a Wisdom saving throw or become frightened of the target for the duration.
A creature frightened in this way can make a Wisdom saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself with a success.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 3rd level or higher, the radius of the aura increases by 10 feet for each slot level above 2nd.

#### Crippling Pain
*3rd-level necromancy*

- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A broken bone)
- **Duration:**  1 round
- **Classes:**  Cleric Warlock, Wizard

You afflict a creature within range with an agonizing curse, causing its body to wither as it's wracked with necrotic energy. The target must make a Constitution saving throw.  On a failed save, it takes 6d6 necrotic damage and is wracked with pain until the end of your next turn.



\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

 On a successful save, the creature takes half the damage and is not affected by the pain.

While wracked with pain, every time the creature takes a move, an action, a bonus action, or a reaction, it takes an additional 3d6 necrotic damage.

***At Higher Levels.***   When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 4th level or higher, the initial damage is increases by 2d6 for each slot level above 3rd.


#### Horrifying Laughter
*6th-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 30 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A tiny tarts and a feather that is waved in the air)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Bard, Wizard
___

You target a creature you can see within range, causing it to collapse into debilitating fits of deranged laughter. The target must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw or fall prone, becoming incapacitated and unable to stand for the duration. Creatures with an Intelligence score of 4 or less aren't affected.

At the end of each of your turns for the duration, any creature within 30 feet of the laughing creature that can hear the laughter must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw or become frightened of the laughing creature until the end of its next turn. You can choose any number of creatures you can see to be immune to this effect.

At the end of each of its turns, the laughing creature takes 3d10 force damage and can attempt another Wisdom saving throw. On a success, the spell ends. If this damage reduces the target to 0 hit points, it stabilizes but remains laughing and can no longer attempt saving throws against the spell. If the spell ends while the creature has 0 hit points, it dies.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 7th level or higher, the damage increases by 1d10 for each slot level above 6th.

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
style='position:absolute;right:-280px;top:-15px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(191deg)' />

#### Impending Doom 
*4th-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A black feather)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Bard, Cleric, Warlock 
___

You target a creature within range, sapping its determination and resolve to go on. The target must make a Charisma saving throw. On a failed save, the creature is filled with a sense of impending doom, and for the duration, whenever it makes an attack roll, ability check, or saving throw against an effect not triggered by this spell, it automatically misses or fails if the roll is 6 or lower, as the creature feels an overwhelming sense of defeat.

The affected creature can make a Charisma saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the spell's effect on a success.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 5th level or higher, you can target one additional creature for each slot level above 4th. The creatures must be within 30 feet of each other when you target them.

#### Purple Sun
*9th-level transmutation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 120 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A pinch of lime, water, and earth)
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard
___

You conjure a grim sphere of purple light at a point you designate within range. The sphere has a maximum radius of 60 feet and illuminates its area with dim light.

Any creature that either enters the sphere's area for the first time on its turn or begins its turn inside the sphere must make a Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, the creature is petrified for the duration. At the end of <br> each of its turns, the target can make another <br> Constitution saving throw. On a success, the <br> spell ends on the target. However, if a creature <br> accumulates three failed saves against this <br> spell (including the initial failed save), it <br> remains petrified indefinitely until the <br> condition is cured by other means.

If a petrified creature is physically <br> damaged or broken during this state, it <br> will manifest the same damage upon <br> being reverted to its original form.

<br>

#### Lore of Shadows: <Br> Art Credit
* Cavalier of Night - Viktor Titov, <br> Wizards of the Coast
* Damnation - Kev Walker, <Br> Wizards of the Coast

\columnbreak

#### Spirit Leech
*1st-level necromancy*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A mosquito)
- **Duration:**  1 hour
- **Classes:**  Warlock
___

You reach out and drain the life force of a target creature you can see within range. The target must make a Charisma saving throw. On a failed save, it takes 1d12 necrotic damage, or half as much on a successful one. You gain temporary hit points equal to the damage dealt. Constructs are immune to this spell's effects.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 2nd level or higher, the damage increases by 1d12 for each slot level above 1st.

#### Wind of Death
*5th-level necromancy*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** Self
- **Components:** V, S, M (A owl feather)
- **Duration:**  Instantaneous
- **Classes:**  Cleric
___

You release unholy wind in a 60-foot-long, 15-foot-wide line in a direction of your choice. Each creature within the line must make a Constitution saving throw. A creature takes 4d6 cold damage and 4d6 necrotic damage on a failed save, and half as much on a success.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 6th level or higher, either the cold or the necrotic damage (your choice) increases by 1d6 for each slot level above 5th.

## Lore of Shadow
This magic specializes in trickery, illusion, <br> and twisting the minds of its targets. Its <br> users primarily rely on illusory magic, though <br> they also wield spells that manipulate shadows <br> and even the nature of space and time as others <br> are able to perceive it, constantly leaving their <br> foes seconding guessing what they're seeing. <br> The following spells are examples of the types <br> of magic users of the Lore of Shadow often wield.

#### Creeping Strike 
*Evocation cantrip*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 10 feet
- **Components:** V S
- **Duration:** Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard
___

You lash out at an enemy with chilling shadows. <Br> Make a melee spell attack against the target. You <Br> have  advantage on the attack roll if the target is in <Br> darkness. On a hit, the target takes 1d8 cold damage.

***At Higher Levels.*** This spell’s damage increases by 1d8 when you reach 5th level (2d8), 11th level (3d8), and 17th level (4d8).

#### Mindrazors
*5th-level illusion*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 bonus action
- **Range:** 30 ft
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Warlock, Bard
___

You envelop up to three weapons you can see within range in phantasmal shadows, allowing them to slice through the minds of their targets. For the duration, when a creature is hit by an attack from one of these infused weapons, it takes an additional 1d12 psychic damage.

If a creature takes an action to examine one of the weapons and succeeds on an Intelligence (Investigation) check against your spell save DC, they discern the illusion and will no longer take the additional psychic damage from any of the infused weapons.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 6th level or higher, you can target one additional weapon for each slot level above 5th.

#### Mirror Dance
*2nd-level conjuration*

- **Casting Time:** 1 bonus action
- **Range:** Self 
- **Components:** S
- **Duration:** Instantaneous
- **Classes:**  Bard, Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard

You weave a shadowy link between yourself and a willing creature you can see within 30 feet, causing you and the creature to instantly swap places. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

> ##### New Condition: Quickened
> A quickened creature gains an additional action on each of its turns. That action can be used only to take the Attack (one weapon attack or unarmed strike only), Dash, Disengage, Hide, or Use an Object action. The *haste* spell applies the quickened condition among its other effects, and a creature cannot benefit from the quickened condition from multiple sources at once.

<br>

The creature must be no more than one size category larger than you. The spell fails if either of you would appear in a space that cannot accommodate your size.

#### Mystifying Miasma
*2nd-level illusion*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 120 ft
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Ranger, Bard
___

You conjure a 20-foot-radius sphere of illusory fog at a point you choose within range. 


 This miasma fills the air, spreading around corners and making the area heavily obscured for all creatures lacking true sight.

Any creature that starts its turn fully within the cloud must make a Wisdom saving throw. On a failed save, it uses its movement to travel in a random direction, determined by rolling a d8, until it exits the fog, after which it falls prone. The creature can then take the rest of its turn as normal.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 3rd level or higher, the radius of the fog increases by 20 feet for each slot level above 2nd.

#### Lore of Shadow: Art Credit
* Myrkul's Invoker - Aaron J. Riley, Wizards of the Coast
* The Abyss - Pete Venters, Wizards of the Coast

#### Penumbral Pendulum
*4th-level illusion*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 120 ft
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:** 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Wizard
___

You conjure a spectral pendulum that swings through a 60-foot-long, 5-foot-wide, and 5-foot-tall line of your choice within range. Each creature in this area can make a Dexterity or Intelligence saving throw (its choice). A creature takes 6d10 psychic damage on a failed save and no damage on a success.

On each of your subsequent turns during the spell's duration, you can use your action to cause the pendulum to swing back from the opposite direction it swang last, repeating the effect across the same line each time. If your turn ends without you using this action, the spell ends.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 5th level or higher, the damage increases by 1d10 for each slot.

#### Pit of Shadows
*6th-level abjuration*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (A black cloth)
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Cleric, Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard
___

You conjure a portal to a shadowy plane, opening a 20-foot square pit on an area of the ground you can see within range. Creatures within this area must make a Dexterity saving  throw. On a failed save, a creature is banished to a realm of darkness for the spell's duration. While in this realm, the creature is incapacitated.

At the end of each of its turns, the banished creature takes 3d8 psychic damage and must then make a Charisma saving throw. On a success, the spell ends for that creature. When the spell ends for a creature, it reappears in its original space or the nearest unoccupied space if its original space is occupied. If a creature dies while banished, its body remains in the shadow realm; however, any magical items it was wearing or carrying return to the original location.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 7th level or higher, you can increase the pit's dimensions by 10 feet for each slot level above 6th.

#### Shroud of Dusk
*1st-level evocation*
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** Self
- **Components:** V, M (A drop of pitch or piece of coal)
- **Duration:**  1 round
- **Classes:**   Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard
___

You release a surge of chilling shadows in a 15-foot-long, 5-foot-wide line that extends from you in a direction you choose. Each creature within the line must make a Constitution saving throw. Creatures take 1d10 cold damage, and on a failed save, and half as much on a success.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

The the line's area is then plunged into magical darkness until the end of your next turn. This darkness is impenetrable to darkvision and unaffected by nonmagical light sources.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 2nd level or higher, the damage increases by 1d10 and the length of the line extends by an additional 5 feet for each slot level above 1st.



#### Unseen Lurker
*3rd-level transmutation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 bonus action
- **Range:** 60 ft
- **Components:** V
- **Duration:** 1 round
- **Classes:**  Ranger
___

Choose a willing creature you can see within range. The chosen creature becomes enveloped in a shroud of mist, enabling it to move with unseen swiftness. Until the start of your next turn, the creature's movement speed is doubled, it's quickened*, and it becomes invisible along with everything it's wearing or carrying.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 5th level or higher, you can target one additional creature for every two slot levels above 3rd.

**New condition described on previous page*

#### Withering Resolve
*3rd-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 120 ft
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Bard
___

Choose a creature within range that can hear you. The target must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw, or its mind becomes filled with crippling doubt and inner turmoil. On a failed save, for the duration of the spell, the target has disadvantage on all checks and saving throws not triggered by this spell, and attack rolls against it have advantage. At the end of each of its turns, the target can make another Wisdom saving throw, ending the effects on a success.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 4th level or higher, you can target one additional creature for each slot level above 3rd.

 <img src='https://i.ibb.co/hDpWQz9/TheAbyss.png' style='position:absolute;right:-0px;top:-20px;width:450px;transform:scaleX(-1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
style='position:absolute;right:-100px;top:-67px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(180deg)' />

## Lore of The Wild
This magic taps into the savage and primeval <br> aspects of nature that have plagued humanity <br> since the dawn of time. Some of these spells <br> conjure the most monstrous aspects of the wild, <br> while others undo the thin veneer of civility that <br> separates humans and their "domestic" creatures <br> from barbaric savagery. This magic is often wielded <br> by those who wish to undo civilization and return <br> everything to a  state of primitive barbarism. The following spells are examples of the types of magic users of the Lore <br> of The Wild often wield.


#### Devolve
*1st-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 30 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (A bit of lizard brain)
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Bard, Druid, Sorcerer

You choose a creature you can see within range. It must succeed on an Intelligence saving throw or be overwhelmed by the primal aspects of its psyche for the duration of the spell. Constructs and undead are immune to this effect. 

While affected, the creature:
* Has disadvantage on Intelligence and Charisma checks
* Cannot cast or concentrate on spells
* Cannot activate magic items
* Cannot speak or understand any language
* Is treated as a beast with an Intelligence score of 4 when targeted by spells and abilities that normally only target beasts, such as *dominate beast* or *beast bond* (This doesn't change its actual Intelligence score)

At the end of each of its turns, the target can make another Intelligence saving throw. On a successful save, the spell ends for that creature.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a 2nd-level spell slot, the affected creature takes 1d10 psychic damage at the end of each of its turns while under this spell's effects before it makes the saving throw. When cast this spell using a spell slot of 3rd level or higher, the psychic damage increases by 1d10 for each slot level above 2nd.


\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

#### Mad Rampage

*4th-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 feet
- **Components:**  V, S, M (a stinger)
- **Duration:**  1 minute
- **Classes:**   Bard, Sorcerer, Warlock
___

You plunge a willing creature within range that you can see into a frenzied state, making it reckless and heedless of danger. 

For the duration of the spell:
* The creature incurs a −2 penalty to AC and Dexterity saving throws.
* The creature becomes quickened.
* When the creature hits with a melee weapon attack or unarmed strike, it deals an additional die of its damage. If the creature moves at least 10 feet in a straight line immediately before making the attack, the attack deals two additional dice of its damage, and it scores a critical hit on a roll of 19 or 20.

If the creature is charmed or frightened, these effects are suspended for the duration of this spell.

#### Mystic Signal

*5th-level transmutation (ritual)*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** self
- **Components:**  V, S, M (A focus worth at <br> least 500 gp, such as a war horn, marble <br> bird, or a gem encrusted jaw bone)
- **Duration:**  1 round
- **Classes:**  Bard, Cleric, Druid, Ranger, Wizard
___

This spell enables you to broadcast a brief message, no longer than four seconds in length, to each creature within 3 miles of your location. Recipients of the message hear it in their minds and, if they know you, recognize you as the sender. Additionally, they discern your distance and direction at the time of casting. The spell ensures that creatures with an Intelligence score of at least 1 can comprehend the message's meaning. 

A sleeping creature can hear the message and may choose to awaken upon hearing it.

You can tailor the spell to target specific types of creatures only, such as humans, giants, unicorns, etc.

The message cannot be received by any creature if there is any thickness of lead, even a thin sheet, blocking a direct path between you and the creature.

#### Primal Scream
*3rd-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (A goat hair)
- **Duration:**   Instantaneous
- **Classes:**  Druid, Bard
___

You or a willing creature of your choice within range is filled with primal vigor and releases a powerful howling roar in a 30-foot cone. If the target is prone, it can immediately stand up without using any movement. Each creature in the cone must make a Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 3d8 thunder damage and is knocked prone. On a success, a creature takes half as much damage and isn’t knocked prone.

Additionally, the creature releasing the roar regains 3d8 hit points. Constructs and undead cannot regain hit points from this spell.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 4th level or higher, both the damage and healing increase by 1d8 for each slot level above 3rd.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

#### Savage Dominion

*7th-level conjuration*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 30 feet
- **Components:**  V, S
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 hour
- **Classes:**   Druid, Warlock
___

You call forth a formidable creature of your choice: a **Stone Hurling Giant**, a **Madding Jabberwocky**, or a **Hungering Behemoth**. It materializes in an unoccupied space within range and vanishes when reduced to 0 hit points or when the spell ends.

This primitive creature is allied with you and your companions. It acts on your initiative count, taking its turn immediately after yours. You can telepathically communicate with the creature while you are on the same plane, and you are both aware of each other's locations. It follows your telepathic commands without requiring an action from you. If not given any commands, it automatically moves toward and attacks the nearest creature it detects.

If the creature moves more than 100 feet from you, your concentration on the spell is broken. Additionally, at the start of its turn, if the creature has taken damage since its last turn, you must succeed on a DC 10 Constitution saving throw or lose concentration.

If your concentration is broken, the creature doesn't disappear but becomes stunned until the end of its next turn, and you lose control over it. The uncontrolled creature cannot be dismissed by you and will disappear 1 hour after it was summoned.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 8th level or higher, the summoned creature gains an additional 25 hit points for each slot level above 7th. If cast using a 9th-level slot, the spell's duration extends to 8 hours.

#### Traitor-Kin

*3rd-level enchantment*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 feet
- **Components:**  V, S, M (a stinger)
- **Duration:**  1 round
- **Classes:**   Bard, Druid, Ranger
___

You choose a beast, monstrosity, giant, dragon, or fey within range that can see and hear you with an Intelligence score of 7 or lower and instill it with a surge of betrayal, compelling it to attack its allies. The creature must succeed on a Wisdom saving throw or become charmed by you until the end of your next turn. 

While charmed this way, all attack rolls against it have advantage, it cannot take reactions or bonus actions, and on the creature's next turn, you may dictate another creature for it to attack (no action required). On its turn, the charmed creature must move towards the chosen target by the safest route possible if it is aware of where the chosen creature is, and it must use its Attack action to make all its attacks against the target, which are made with advantage. If it is unaware of the chosen creature's location, it does nothing on its turn.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a 4th-level spell slot or higher, you can target one additional creature for each slot level above 3rd.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

#### Vile Tide
*2nd-level conjuration*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 60 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M  (A few grains of sugar, some kernels of grain, and a smear of fat)
- **Duration:**   Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Cleric, Druid, Sorcerer
___

You cause a swarm of insects to erupt from the ground within a 10-foot square area at a point you choose within range. Each creature standing in this area must make a Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 4d4 piercing damage, and insects burrow into the creature, remaining there for the spell's duration. On a successful save, a creature takes half the initial damage, and the insects do not burrow into it. 

While the insects are burrowed in a creature, the creature has disadvantage on checks, cannot regain hit points, and takes 2d4 piercing damage at the end of each of its turns. 

Any creature within reach can use an action to perform a Wisdom (Medicine) check against your spell save DC to try to remove the insects from a creature. This check must be done using a weapon or object that deals fire, piercing, or slashing damage, and it causes 1d4 damage of its damage type to the target. On a successful check, all the insects are destroyed, and the spell ends for that creature. The creature making the check can choose to gain advantage by more aggressively trying to remove the insects, but if it does, the target takes 3d4 damage instead. 

Alternatively, a creature can expend a use of a Healer's Kit or use the *lesser restoration* spell to purge the insects without needing to make a check.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 3rd level or higher, the initial damage increases by 2d4 for each slot level above 2nd.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/3mF4gB5/carrion-beatles.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-100px; right:-0px; width:820px; transform: scaleX(1)' />

> ## Hungering Behemoth
> *Huge monstrosity, unaligned*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 15 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 150
> - **Speed** 40 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|22 (+6)|6 (-2)|20 (+5)|7 (-2)|8 (-1)|8 (-1)|
>___
> - **Senses** passive Perception 9
> - **Languages** Abyssal
> - **Challenge** 8 (3,900 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&ensp; **Proficiency Bonus** +3
> ___
>
> ***Charge.*** If the behemoth moves at least 20 feet straight toward a target and then hits it with a Gore attack on the same turn, the target takes an extra 11 (2d10) piercing damage. If the target is a creature, it must succeed on a Strength saving throw against your spell save DC or be pushed up to 10 feet away and knocked prone.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The behemoth makes two attacks.
>
> ***Rend.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* your spell attack modifier to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 21 (3d10 + 5) slashing damage. If the target is reduced to 0 hit points by the attack, the behemoth may make another Rend attack against a different creature within 10 feet of the original target and within range of this attack. The behemoth does not gain another attack if it reduces the new target to 0 hit points.
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* your spell attack modifier to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 21 (3d10 + 5) piercing.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* your spell attack modifier to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 21 (3d10 + 5) piercing, and the target is grappled (escape DC equal to your spell save). Until this grapple ends, the target is restrained, and the behemoth can't bite another target. If the target is a Large or smaller and already grappled by the behemoth, the target is swallowed, and the grapple ends. The swallowed target is blinded and restrained, it has total cover against attacks and other effects outside the behemoth, and it takes 18 (4d8) acid damage at the start of each of the behemoth's turns. If the behemoth dies, a swallowed creature is no longer restrained by it and can escape from the corpse by using 20 feet of movement, exiting prone.
>

> ## Stone Hurling Giant
> *Huge giant, unaligned*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 15 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 150
> - **Speed** 40 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|22 (+6)|12 (+1)|20 (+5)|7 (-2)|10 (0)|8 (-1)|
>___
> - **Senses** passive Perception 10
> - **Languages** Giant
> - **Challenge** 8 (3,900 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&ensp; **Proficiency Bonus** +3
> ___
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The giant makes a fist attack and a stomp attack.
>
> ***Fist.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* your spell attack modifier to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 23 (4d8 + 5) bludgeoning damage. Instead of dealing damage, the giant can choose grapple the target (escape DC equal to your spell save) provided the target is Huge or smaller. The giant has two fists, each of which can grapple only one target.
>
> ***Stomp.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* your spell attack modifier to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 16 (2d10 + 5) bludgeoning damage. If the target is a prone creature or Medium or smaller in size, it takes 27 (4d10 + 5) instead.
>
> ***Fling.***  The giant chooses one object or creature it is holding or grappling that is its size or smaller and throws it up to 120 feet away. If the target lands on a solid surface, it takes 21 (3d10 + 5) damage and lands prone. If the thrown creature or object would land in the space of one or more creatures, each of those creatures must make a Dexterity save against your spell save DC. On a failed save, a creature is hit by the thrown creature, takes 21 (3d10 + 5) bludgeoning damage, and is knocked prone. On a successful save, it dodges out of the way, takes no damage, and is not knocked prone.
>

> ## Maddening Jabberwocky
> *Huge dragon, unaligned*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 15 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 150
> - **Speed** 40 ft, fly 40 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|22 (+6)|12 (+1)|20 (+5)|7 (-2)|10 (0)|8 (-1)|
>___
> - **Senses** passive Perception 10
> - **Languages** Draconic
> - **Challenge** 8 (3,900 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&ensp; **Proficiency Bonus** +3
> ___
>
> ***Burble.*** At the end of the jabberwocky's turn, each creature within 30 feet of it that can hear it must make a Wisdom saving against you spell save DC. On a failed save, a creature is frightened until the start of its next turn. While frightened this way, it is dazed. If a creature’s saving throw is successful, it is immune to the Burble of the jabberwocky for the next hour.
>
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The jabberwocky makes two attacks.
>
> ***Dripping Jaws.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* your spell attack modifier to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 15 (2d8 + 6) piercing damage and the target covered in acid for one minute or until a creature uses its action to scrape or wash the acid off itself or another creature. A creature covered in the acid takes 5 (2d4) acid damage at the end of each of its turns.
>
> ***Snatching Claws.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* your spell attack modifier to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 15 (2d8 + 6) slashing damage. The target is grappled (escape DC equal to your spell save throw). The jabberwocky has two claws, each of which can grapple only one target.
>
> ***Eyes of Flame.*** The jabberwocky shoots a beam of fire from its eyes in a 30-foot line that is 5 feet wide. Each creature in the line's area must make a Dexterity save against your spell save DC. On a failed save, a creature takes 10 (4d4) fire damage and is set on fire; until a creature uses its action to douse the fire on itself or another creature, the target takes 5 (2d4) fire damage at the end of each of its turns. On a successful save, a creature takes half as much damage and is not set on fire.

## Beastman Magic Items
Most beastmen don't take part in crafting anything beyond the crudest weaponry as they are more inclined towards destruction than creation. However, they often acquire powerful magical items by twisting the creations of others or finding dark sources of power in the wild that can be formed into imposing weapons. The following magic items reflect some of the creations that can be found in their possession.


### Axe of Man-Slaying 
*Weapon (Greataxe), Uncommon (Requires Attunement), 1,000 gp*  

*The Axe of Man-Slaying earned its name for its ability to cleave even the largest warrior in twain as easily as a hot knife cuts through butter. This fearsome weapon slices with terrifying ease, its effortless carving through the strongest foes a stupefying—and horrifying—sight that emboldens allies while breaking enemies.*

When you roll a 20 on an attack roll made with this weapon, the target takes an extra 20 slashing damage. If a creature has 20 Hit Points or fewer after taking this damage, it is cut in half and dies. If a creature dies this way, each enemy in a 60-foot emanation from you must succeed on a DC 15 Wisdom saving throw or be frightened of you for the next minute. A frightened creature takes the Dash action and moves away from you by the safest route on each of its turns unless there is nowhere to move. If the creature ends its turn in a space where it doesn’t have line of sight to you, it makes a Wisdom saving throw. On a successful save, the effect ends on that creature. Additionally, each ally in the emanation may end any frightened condition affecting them.


<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>


### The Black Star

*Weapon (Morningstar), Very Rare (Requires Attunement), 16,000 gp*

*The cudgel was forged from the remnants of a meteorite that crashed down from the heavens, unleashing a wave of madness upon impact. Those who take up this hulking weapon find its spirit granting them visions of mayhem and slaughter—causing the wielder’s mind to drown in insanity.*

When you roll Initiative while holding this weapon, you can choose to have the weapon gain up to three charges until the end of combat. The weapon gets +1 to attack rolls and deals an additional 1d8 dice of damage for each charge it has. Additionally, at the start of each of your turns, even if you are not holding the weapon, you roll a number of d6s on the Madness Effects Table (found at the end of the document) equal to the number of charges on the weapon to determine your actions during the turn.


### Horn of the First Beast

*Wonderous Item (Instrument), Rare (Requires Attunement), 12,800 gp*

*This fossilized horn belonged to the first beast birthed from the twisting power of Chaos, when its corruption first took hold in the mortal realm. When blown, it releases an ancient roar that fills those who hear it with primeval fury.*

As an action, you can blow this horn, causing each ally within 60 feet to become Emboldened*. Once you use the horn, it can’t be used again until the next dawn. When the horn is sounded, it can be heard clearly up to a mile away.

**New condition described at the end of the section*

### Horn of the Great Hunt

*Wonderous Item (Instrument), Very Rare <Br> (Requires Attunement), 60,000 gp*

*Said to have been fashioned from the tusk of a dead boar god, this horn has been used by beastmen for generations in their foul conquests. When sounded, the entire warband surges forward with predatory fervor.*

When you roll Initiative and are not incapacitated or surprised while holding the horn, you may blow it. If you do, any number of allies within 120 feet of you that can hear the horn, and are not surprised or incapacitated, also roll Initiative and gain a +5 bonus to their roll. Their speed then increases by 20 feet for their first turn in combat. When the horn is sounded, it can be heard clearly up to a mile away.


### Hunting Spear

*Weapon (Spear), Rare (Requires Attunement), 4,800 gp*

*This thick-shafted hunting spear was crafted to fell the mighty beasts of the frozen wastes. The enchantments infused within it surge with power when the weapon is hurled, increasing its velocity and impact force.*

You gain a +2 bonus to attack and damage rolls made with this magic weapon. In addition, attacking at long range with this weapon doesn’t impose disadvantage on the attack rolls, and the weapon deals an extra 2d6 piercing damage on hit if the attack was made at long range.


### Mind Mangler

*Weapon (Scimitar), Rare (Requires Attunement), 4,000 gp*

*Said to have once been a sentient weapon, its mind was shattered when its master attempted to use it to slay the hideous jabbersnarl brood mother of the ancient wood. The broken remnants of the blade’s consciousness—and twisted reflections of the revolting abomination—are still woven into its metal. Any struck by it have their minds assaulted by demented thoughts and maddening visions.*

At the end of your turn, you may choose one creature you hit with this weapon on this turn and force it to make a DC 15 *Intelligence Saving Throw*. <Br> *Failure:* The creature can’t take reactions until the start of its next turn and rolls a number of d4s on the Madness Effects Table below equal to the number of times it was hit with the weapon this turn.


\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>


### Primeval Club

*Weapon (Club), Very Rare (Requires Attunement), 18,000 gp*

*This simple branch, wrapped in crude skins, is said to be a weapon fashioned in the distant past by the first tribes of humans who inhabited the deepest woods—long before villages and cities dotted the landscape. Those of truly feral nature are able to wield this club, delivering savage blows with primal force.*

While you aren’t wearing heavy armor or wielding a shield, you gain a +3 bonus to attack rolls made with this magic weapon, and when you hit with an attack using this weapon, the target takes an extra 2d4 bludgeoning damage. In addition, you can use your Wisdom instead of Strength for the attack and damage rolls of melee attacks using this weapon.

### Ram Horn Helm
*Wonderous Item, Rare (Requires Attunement), 4,000 gp*

*The helm was fashioned from a pair of thick, coiling horns taken from a particularly dreadful beastlord, slain by a rival who wished to add the impressive horns to his own regalia. The wearer of this mantle is able to charge into enemy lines with bone-cracking force.*

While wearing this helm, you gain a +1 bonus to AC. Additionally, once per turn, if you move 20+ feet straight toward a target before hitting it with a melee weapon attack, the target takes an extra 2d6 bludgeoning damage and must succeed on a DC 15 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone.

<img src='https://i.postimg.cc/7ZKMnV9R/Signal-The-Clans.jpg' style='position:absolute;top:-10px;right:-18px;width:920px; transform: scaleX(-1) rotate(-0deg)' />

### Rod of the Chattering Skull

*Rod, Uncommon (Requires Attunement),  1,000 gp*

*Once, a mighty bray-speaker tenaciously sought to master the dark arts to a degree no other disciple of Chaos ever had. So merciless was his pursuit of this twisted desire that he spiraled into lunacy. Ultimately, the shaman became so unhinged that his own tribe was forced to decapitate him. Now, the bray-speaker’s bleached skull is fastened to a crude rod, its jaws chattering as it imparts the maddening knowledge it gathered in life.*

The rod has 6 charges and regains 1d4 + 2 of its expended charges daily at dawn.

When you or a willing creature you can see within 60 feet of you that can see and hear you fails a saving throw while you're holding the rod, you can use your reaction to expend a charge to roll up to 3d6 and add the number rolled to the d20, potentially turning the failure into a success. On the creature's next turn, the creature performs the action on the Madness Effects Table (found at the end of the document) equal to the number added to the saving throw.

### Sacrificial Dagger

*Weapon (Dagger, Holy Symbol, Arcane Focus, Druidic Focus), Rare (Requires Attunement by a Bard, Cleric, Druid, Sorcerer, Warlock, or Wizard), 10,000 gp*

*A rough-hewn blade, stained with the blood of thousands of sacrifices. Any who add to the countless lives it has claimed will be greatly rewarded.*

You gain a +1 bonus to attack and damage rolls made with this magic weapon. Additionally, when you deal damage to a creature with a CR or class level of 1 or higher with this weapon, if it has 15 Hit Points or fewer after taking the damage, it dies and the blade gains a charge. The dagger can hold up to 5 charges.

While holding the dagger, you can use an action to expend some of its charges to cast one of the following spells from it, using your spell save DC: *aspect of dread* (2 charges), *crippling pain* (4 charges), *wind of death* (5 charges).

**New spell described in Spells section*

### Shredder Claws

*Weapon (Sickle), Rare (Requires Attunement), 5,000 gp*

*Many elegant elven swords were shattered to create this set of vicious claws, each blade pilfered from the mangled corpse of a mighty elven warrior and transmuted into one of the wicked fingers of this deadly apparatus. The claws can tear through anything they are set against, limited only by the fury of their wielder.*

The weapon comes in a pair, which the creature must have both of to attune to and counts as one attunement.

When you roll the weapon’s damage dice for an attack you make with either weapon, for each 4 you roll, the weapons deal an additional 1d8 damage on any further attacks you make this turn with either one. Additionally, when you score a critical hit with either weapon, instead of rolling all of your damage dice twice and adding them together, you treat the d4 roll as a 4.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

### Staff of Swarming Insects (Revised)

*Staff, Very Rare (Requires Attunement by a Bard, Cleric, Druid, Sorcerer, Warlock, or Wizard), 16,000 gp*

*The staff teems with all manner of invertebrates that endlessly scuttle up and down its surface, waiting to be unleashed at the command of its bearer.*

This staff has 10 charges and regains 1d6 + 4 expended charges daily at dawn.

**Spells.** While holding the staff, you can use an action to expend some of its charges to cast one of the following spells from it, using your spell save DC: *fog cloud* (1 charge, the cloud appears as a swarm of insects), *vile tide** (2 charges), *giant insect* (4 charges), or *insect plague* (5 charges).

**New spell described in Spells section*

### Madness Effects Table  

| Number Rolled | Name        | Effect |
|:---:|:-----------|:-----------|
|  1  | Stable     | The creature acts as normal. |
|  2  | Agitated    | The creature must take the Attack action or cast a spell that deals damage. |
|  3  | Fixated    | The creature must spend 2 feet of movement for every 1 foot it moves when moving away from any creatures hostile to it that it is aware of. |
|  4  | Trepidation | The creature must spend 2 feet of movement for every 1 foot it moves when moving closer to any creatures hostile to it that it is aware of. |
|  5  | Paranoid   | The creature considers no other creature an ally, refusing help and being unable to benefit from the spells and effects of allies. |
|  6  | Lonely    | The creature has disadvantage on attack rolls and checks unless it is within 5 feet of an ally that isn't incapacitated. |
|  7  | Dizzy      | The creature uses half it's movement to travel in a random direction, determined by rolling a d8. It can then take the rest of its turn as normal. |
|  8  | Babble     | The creature yells at the top of its lungs. It can't cast spells with verbal components, speak, eat, or drink until the start of its next turn. |
| 9  | Blurred Vision     | The creatrue unable to see anything farther than 10 feet away until the start of it's next turn. |

<br>

> ##### New Condition:  Dazed 
> A dazed creature can’t take reactions and on its turn, it must choose whether it gets a move, an action, or a bonus action; it gets only one of the three.

\columnbreak

<br><br>

| Number Rolled | Name        | Effect |
|:---:|:-----------|:-----------|
|  10  | Dull-Witted | The creature can make only one attack during the turn and can only cast cantrips. |
| 11  | Huddle     | The creature falls prone and can't stand up for the rest of its turn. |
| 12  | Addled     | Until the end of the turn, the creature is dazed (condition described below) and can't concentrate. |
| 13  | Frantic    | The creature must take the Dash, Dodge, or Disengage action this turn. |
| 14  | Shivers    | The creature drops whatever it is holding. It can't pick up items, wield weapons, or cast spells with somatic components. |
| 15  | Denial     | The creature can't see or hear any creatures hostile to it until the start of its next turn. |
| 16  | Violent   | The creature moves toward the nearest creature it is aware of and then uses its action to make a single attack if the target is within range. |
| 17  | Penance    | The creature uses it's action to make an attack with whatever it is holding against itself, automatically hitting. |
| 18+  | Catatonia | The creature is stunned until the start of its next turn. |

<br>

> ##### New Condition: Emboldened  
> This document references the Emboldened condition. 
> * The Emboldened condition always lasts one minute.
> * An Emboldened creature deals additional 7 (2d6) damage when it hits with a attack.
> * At the end of the creature's turn, the Emboldened condition ends early if it missed with all of its attacks that turn, it is charmed or frightened, or is effected by *calm emotions* spell. 
>

# The Warherd
This section lists the different <br> types of beastmen along with <br> the savage monsters they <br> often utilize in battle. The <br> different types of beastmen <br> include the shorthorns, <br> longhorns, and besthorns. The <br> various horrific monsters they utilize can be <br> found living alongside the beastmen or lurking <br> the wilds of their dark forest homelands. 

## Chaos Mutations

The twisting power of Chaos carries an unpredictable <br> quality in its corruption, bestowing a wide range of <br> deadly traits upon individuals. In places where Chaos <br> has deeply seeped into the land, there are records of monsters unlike anything seen elsewhere in the <br> world—wolf-like creatures with jagged beaks whose <br> saliva can dissolve metal; massive predatory cats that <br> melt into shadows and scale the sheer stone walls of fortresses to feed on inhabitants within; and even strange, wicked humanoids with hides thicker than leather, constantly shifting and warping to ward off attack. Accounts of these bizarre deviations and their horrific exploits are numerous. Yet no two records ever share a description of the exact same miscreation.

The following mechanics provide various mutations you can apply to existing creatures to represent the warping effect Chaos (or any other power appropriate to your setting) has had on that creature. This can provide surprise twists on creatures players are familiar with that challenge them in new ways and meaningfully display the power of Chaos to distort everything it touches.

**CR Increase.** Applying a mutation increases a creature's CR by 1 (fractional CRs are doubled, e.g., a CR 1/4 creature becomes CR 1/2.)

**Mutation Save DC.** If a mutation force a creature to make a Saving throw or check, the DC is equal to 10 + it's Proficiency Bonus

### General Mutations
The following is a list of mutations that can be applied to any creature to represent the effects the constant mutating power of chaos can have on them. The creature receiving the mutation is referred to as the "mutant."

To pick a mutation at random, roll 1d20 and match the result to the number of the mutation.

#### 1. Acidic Secretions

*The beast’s claws, teeth, or other natural weapons drip with corrosive fluids, capable of reducing a victim to a delectable slurry should the caustic substance make contact.*

Choose one of the mutant's natural weapons to become enhanced.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

Once per turn when the mutant hits with the enhanced weapon, the target takes an extra 10 (3d6) acid damage and the creature is covered in acid until it or a creature uses its action to scrape or wash the acid off. While covered in acid, it takes 10 (3d6) acid damage at the end of each of its turns.


#### 2. Adaptive Defense

*Should one manage to wound the beast, its body begins to twist and change. Within seconds, it adapts into a new form impervious to the attacker’s strikes.*

The mutant gains the following Reaction:

***Adaptive Defense (Recharges after a Short or Long Rest).*** *Trigger:* When the mutant takes damage. *Response:* The mutant becomes immune to the triggering damage type for the next minute. (This does not negate the damage that triggered the reaction.)


#### 3. Earth-Ripping Claws

*With massive paws or chitinous blades, the beast moves through the earth like a fish through water. Lurking below, it waits for the telltale vibrations of prey above before it strikes.*

The mutant has a burrow speed of 20 feet and Tremorsense out to 30 feet.


#### 4. Expeditious Metabolism

*The creature can digest blood, flesh, and bone within seconds, rapidly converting the carnage into fuel to restore its own body.*

Choose one of the mutant's natural weapons to become enhanced.

Once per turn when the mutant hits with the enhanced weapon, it regains 20 hit points.

* Skophos Reaver - Andrew Mar, Wizards of the Coast

#### 5. Gnarled Hide

*The beast's hide has toughened up to the point that it serves as a layer of living armor.*

The mutant gets +3 to its AC


#### 6. Gouging Tusks

*The beast has a large pair of tusks sprouting from its lower jaw, granting it an even more devastating charge attack.*

Choose one of the mutant's natural weapons to become enhanced.

Once per turn, if the mutant has moved 20+ feet straight toward a target immediately before it hits with the enhanced weapon, the target takes an extra 17 (5d6) piercing damage.


#### 7. Many Limbed Monster

*The beast sports an extra pair of limbs to tear at its enemies.*

Choose one of the mutant's natural weapons.

When the mutant takes the Attack action, it makes one additional attack as part of the action, which uses the attack modifier of the chosen weapon for the attack roll. On hit, the target takes 14 (4d6) slashing damage.


#### 8. Regeneration

*No amount of slicing, stabbing, or thrashing will keep it down for long. Muscles regrow, skin stitches itself closed, bones snap back into place—and the beast rises once more.*

The mutant regains 15 hit points at the start of its turn. If the mutant takes fire or acid damage, this trait doesn't function at the start of the mutant's next turn. The mutant dies only if it starts its turn with 0 hit points and doesn't regenerate.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

> ##### Using Mutations To Create Urgency In Adventures
> If you're running an adventure that focuses heavily on encounters with beastmen and you want to create a sense of urgency, you can have the beastmen in the adventure gain mutations as time passes. This means the more slowly and carefully the players progress, the more dangerous the beastmen will become. This can help keep the players from playing too conservatively. 
> 
> If you want the mutations to be random, you can roll a d8 to determine what mutation they will gain (number each of the abilities in alphabetical order).
>
> The rate at which they gain mutations could be on the scale of hours or days, depending on the scope and pacing of your adventure.
>
<br>

#### 9. Infesting Injector

*The beast can implant parasitic organisms into other creatures—whether they are grotesque organisms it harbors or its own repulsive young.*

Once per turn, when the mutant hits with the enhanced weapon, parasites burrow into target's flesh, infesting it. While infested, the creature takes 10 (3d6) damage. Any creature within reach can use an action to make a DC Wisdom (Medicine) check to remove the parasites using a weapon or object that deals fire, piercing, or slashing damage, causing 1d6 damage of the same type to the target. On a successful check, the effect ends. The creature making the check can choose to gain advantage by more aggressively trying to remove the parasites, but if it does, the target takes 2d6 damage instead.


#### 10. Shadow Hide

*The beast's black fur melds perfectly with the darkness around it, allowing it to stalk its prey from the shadows while completely unseen.*

While in darkness, the mutant is invisible to any creature that relies on darkvision to see it in that darkness. Additionally, it gets a +5 on Dexterity (Stealth) checks and does not suffer disadvantage on checks from wearing armor.

 <img src='https://i.ibb.co/RHGnNx1/thb-109-nyxborn-marauder-cropped.jpg' style='position:absolute;right:0px;top:-75px;width:850px;transform:scaleX(-1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
style='position:absolute;right:-80px;top:99px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(180deg) scaleX(-1)' />

\pagebreakNum

#### 11. Shredding Implement

*The beast’s claws, beak, horns, or other natural weapons grow jagged and barbed, tearing muscles into tattered, useless strands.*

Choose one of the mutant's natural weapons to become enhanced.

Once per turn, when the mutant hits with the enhanced weapon, the target suffers a rending wound. While wounded, the target has disadvantage on Strength, Dexterity, and Constitution d20 Tests, and its speed is halved. The wound ends if the target regains 15 or more hit points at once or if the target, or a creature within 5 feet of it, can use an action to stanch the wound by succeeding on a DC Wisdom (Medicine) check.


#### 12. Slug-Skin

*This beastman's disgusting skin oozes thick, slippery, toxic slime.*

At the end of the mutant's turn, any ground within 5 feet of it is covered in slime for the next minute, causing it to become difficult terrain.

A creature standing on the slime has disadvantage on Dexterity and Strength saving throws, and prone creatures in the area must spend all their movement to stand up instead of half. If a creature ends its turn in the area, it takes 10 (3d6) poison damage. Any creature with this mutation ignores its effects.

\columnbreak

#### 13. Snatching Appendage

*Whether a chameleon-like tongue, mantis-like limbs, or a grotesquely elongated arm, the beast can strike with lightning speed and drag its ill-gotten prize away—screaming.*

Choose one of the mutant's natural weapons to become enhanced.

The enhanced weapon has its reach extended by 15 feet. On hit, the target is grappled and pulled 15 feet towards the creature.


#### 14. Sneak Attack

*Driven by malevolent cunning, the beast exploits even the most minuscule of gaps in its opponents' defenses, striking with terrifying precision.*

Once per turn, the mutant deals an extra 21 (6d6) damage when it hits a target with a weapon attack and has advantage on the attack roll, or when the target is within 5 feet of an ally of the mutant that isn't incapacitated and the mutant doesn't have disadvantage on the attack roll.


#### 15. Splendid Mantle

*This beast is adorned with especially grandiose features—twisting horns, vibrant feathered plumes, or some other majestic trait. Granting it an arrogant confidence, fully aware it has been blessed by the dark gods.*

If the mutant is not bloodied, it gets +5 to all Intelligence, Wisdom, and Charisma saving throws.

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:-360px; right:00px; transform:rotate(180deg); width:900px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%)' />

#### 16. Springing Legs

*The beast can launch itself staggering distances, crashing down upon the unprepared.*

Once per turn, the mutant can jump up to 40 feet by spending 10 feet of movement. If the mutant has jumped 20+ feet straight toward a target immediately before it hits with an attack, it gains advantage on the attack roll.


#### 17. Sticky Smear 

*The beast is able to Release clinging webbing or thick mucus, which immobilize anything caught within.*

Choose one of the mutant's natural weapons to become enhanced.

Once per turn, when the mutant hits with the enhanced weapon, the creature is restrained by sticky mucus or webbing until it is destroyed (AC 15; HP 20; immune to bludgeoning, necrotic, poison, and psychic damage).


#### 18. Uncanny Senses

*The beast's primal senses have been heightened to new levels, allowing it to perceive even the most well-hidden prey and the stealthiest of threats.*

The mutant gets +5 on initiative rolls and Wisdom (Perception) checks and does not suffer disadvantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks in areas that are lightly obscured. It also gains blindsight out to 30 feet.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

#### 19. Unsettling Scuttle

*Insectoid limbs lined with barbed hairs allow the beast to move in an off-putting, unpredictable manner. It skitters effortlessly across any terrain, bypassing foes without pause or penalty.*

The mutant has a climb speed equal to its walking speed and can climb on difficult surfaces, including along ceilings, and doesn't provoke attacks of opportunity.


#### 20. Vile Toxins

*The beast’s venom is so potent that even the slightest scratch can deliver a fatal dose, sapping away life in mere seconds.*

Choose one of the mutant's natural weapons to become enhanced.

Once per turn, when the mutant hits with the enhanced weapon, the target must make a Constitution Saving Throw. *Failure:* The target is poisoned for the next minute. While poisoned, it can't regain hit points. At the end of each of its turns, the poisoned creature repeats the Constitution Saving Throw. *Success:* It ends the poison. *Failure:* It takes 14 (4d6) poison damage.
