### Beastmen  Mutations List

The following is a list of mutations that can only be applied to beastmen. To pick a mutation at random, roll 1d6 and match the result to the number of the mutation.


#### 1. Arcane Fury

*The beastman’s horns act as arcane conduits, drawing in powerful magic and infusing it with potent mystic vigor.*

The beastman gains the following reaction:

 *Trigger:* When another creature within 15 feet of the beastman casts a 1st or higher level spell. *Response:* The beastman becomes Emboldened*. If the beastman already Emboldened, it may move up to half its speed and make a single gore attack. The attack has advantage if it is made against the creature that triggered the ability.



#### 2. Cursed Tongue

*Humility is anathema to the beastman. Should another cause it to appear weak or foolish, it responds by weaving a hex in its foul language—inflicting it upon the source of its shame.*

When the beastman loses the Emboldened* condition from missing with all of its attacks against the same creature on the same turn, it may curse a creature. It may also curse a creature when it loses the Emboldened condition due to being Charmed or Frightened by a creature. The curse lasts for one minute, until the beastman it becomes Emboldened again, or until the beastman dies. While cursed, whenever a target makes a d20 test, the target must subtract 1d6 from the roll. A creature can be cursed this way by more than one beastman at a time, and the effects stack.


#### 3. Disfiguring Hate

*The beastman’s fury warps its visage into a grotesque mask of rage. Its guttural roars of loathing echo forth, while a slick, rancid sweat seeps from its flesh, carrying a stench so hateful it stings the eyes—a living nightmare of repulsion.*


The beastman emits an aura in a 30-foot emanation <br> from itself while it is Emboldened* which forces <br> creatures to make the following saving throw. <br> *Wisdom Saving Throw:* Each enemy that <br> starts its turn in the emanation. <br> *Failure:* The creature is Frightened of <br> all Emboldened creatures until the <br> start of its next turn. 

If a creature would make <br> multiple saving throws against <br> the Disfiguring Hate abilities <br> of multiple beastmen, it instead <br> makes a single saving throw.  <br>The save DC equals the highest <br> save DC among the beastmen plus <br> 2 per saving throw that was forgone.

<br>

**New condition described at the <br> end of the document*

\columnbreak


#### 4. Fetid Soul

*So drenched in festering hatred is the beastman’s spirit that, as it tears free from its corpse in death, the vile essence fouls all it touches—leaving rot and hate in its wake.*

When the beastman dies while it is Emboldened*, it explodes, forcing creatures to make the following saving throw. *Constitution Saving Throw:* Each non-beastman creature within a 10-foot emanation of the beastman when it dies. *Failure:* The creature takes 7 (2d6) necrotic damage and suffers a level of exhaustion. *Success:* Half damage only. 

Each beastman in the emanation becomes Emboldened if it is not already in one.



#### 5. Rune of the Beast

*The beastman has a large eldritch rune carved into its flesh. When it becomes enraged, the rune glows red hot and distorts the flow of magic around it.*

If the beastman fails a saving throw against a spell while Emboldened*, it can choose to end the Emboldened condition and succeed instead. If the beastman would take half damage on a success, it instead takes no damage.

#### 6. Wounded Rage

*Deep wounds and broken bones only drive the beastman to strive harder, dreading the judgment of its dark gods should it die in failure.* 

If the beastman is bloodied and Emboldened, it has advantage on attack rolls, and its attacks deal an additional 7 (2d6) damage on hit.

## Avatar of Beasts

From the echoing roars of ancient beasts to the silent stalk of the predator, nature begets a power all its own, an unchecked and relentless force. It is this raw, untamed energy that gives birth to an elemental known as an avatar of beasts, enigmatic entities born from the very soul of the wilderness.

**Primeval Visage.** These towering creatures walk upon the land with long, powerful strides. Their body is a blend of various animal spirits, giving them an almost unpredictable look, though most are bipedal with a vaguely humanoid body shape. A constant is their skull-like head adorned with antlers that rise like darkened spires. Eyes, pools of haunting luminescence, observe the world with primal intensity. Their vast hooved feet, capable of pulverizing any caught in their step, and their supernatural claws, an embodiment of nature's fury, are weapons of unparalleled savagery. With each individual avatar drawing upon various primal animal spirits, no two are exactly alike. One might have the scales of a serpent intermixed with the fur of a lion, while another might possess the feathery mantle and claws of an eagle combined with the armored hide of a rhino.

**Veil of the Wilds.** Despite their daunting size, avatars of beasts possess an uncanny ability to meld with the wilderness. They move through forests, mountains, and swamps as if they were phantoms, impervious to natural barriers and ever-prepared to ambush the unwary. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

Their harmony with nature allows them to bypass any plant obstructions their forest homes might impose, making them almost impossible to anticipate.

**Supernatural Savagery.** In battle, these elementals are a spectacle of raw might and eldritch power. While their natural weapons—claws, antlers, and hooves—are deadly enough, their supernatural abilities add another level of terror. They can summon flocks of relentless birds whose sharp talons and beaks dive upon foes with murderous intent, often blinding their victims. When their foes amass to charge them head-on, avatars of beasts are even known to unleash rays of eerie and deadly supernatural light, thought to be the essence of the magic that makes up their being.

**Summoning the Beast.** While these elementals are free spirits of the wild, there are those with the knowledge to call upon them. Druids, shamans, and other mystics of the wilderness, in times of sheer desperation, might perform ancient and savage rituals to summon these mighty beings. These ceremonies are not to be taken lightly, often demanding a primeval sacrifice, where the essence of the wild is offered in exchange for the avatar's aid.

 <img src='https://i.ibb.co/NZyHRtH/Old-Stickfingers-Innistrad-Midnight-Hunt-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute;right:-100px;top:-0px;width:1000px;transform:scaleX(-1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
style='position:absolute;right:-93px;top:185px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(192deg)' />

> ## Avatar of Beasts
> *Huge elemental, unaligned*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 17 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 276 (24d12 + 120)
> - **Speed** 50 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|25 (+7)|18 (+4)|20 (+5)|7 (-2)|20 (+5)|16 (+3)|
>___
> - **Skills** Athletics +12, Perception +15, Intimidation +8, Stealth +9, Survival +10
> - **Senses** blindsight 60 ft., darkvision 120 ft., passive Perception 25
> - **Condition Immunities** charmed, frightened
> - **Challenge** 15 (13,000 XP) &emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +5
> ___
>
> ***Crashing Charge.*** If the avatar moves at least 20 ft. straight toward a creature and then hits it with a Gore attack on the same turn, the target takes an extra 11 (2d10) damage. If the target is a creature, it must succeed on a DC 20 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone. The creature makes the saving throw with disadvantage if the attack was made using its Bestial Take Down bonus action.
>
> ***One with the Wild.*** The avatar has advantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made to hide in foliage, heavy rain, falling snow, mist, and other natural phenomena and can do so when only lightly obscured. Additionally, the avatar can move through plants without being slowed, taking damage, or being grappled or restrained by them, and can move through trees as if they were difficult terrain. It takes 10 force damage if it ends its turn inside a tree.
>
> ***Primal Senses.*** The avatar has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks and does not suffer disadvantage on the checks in areas that are lightly obscured.
>
> ***Talons of the Forest.*** When the avatar makes an attack, it ignores half and three-quarters cover provided by foliage.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The avatar makes two attacks.
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +12 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 23 (3d10 + 7) piercing damage.
>
> ***Savage Talons.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +12 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 23 (3d10 + 7) slashing damage plus 11 (2d10) for each time this turn the target has already been hit with its Talon attack this turn.
>
> ***Pulverizing Stomp.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +12 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 23 (3d10 + 7) bludgeoning damage. If the target is a prone creature, it cannot stand up until the end of the avatar's next turn unless it uses its action to succeed on a DC 20 Constitution check.
>
> ***Amber Breath (1/day).*** The avatar exhales amber light in a 60-foot line that is 15 feet wide. Each creature in that area must make a DC 18 Dexterity saving throw, taking 27 (5d10) radiant damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one. The creatures gain no benefit from cover given by foliage for this saving throw.
>
> ***Flock of Doom.*** The avatar fills a 20-foot-radius sphere centered on a point within 100 feet of it with shadowy crows. The avatar can designate any number of creatures it is aware of to be unaffected by the crows. The sphere spreads around corners, and it lasts until the avatar uses the ability again, is more than 100 feet away from the area, or loses concentration (as if concentrating on a spell). The sphere's area is difficult terrain, and creatures in it have disadvantage on ranged attack rolls. At the end of each of the avatar's turns, each creature in the area must make a DC 18 Dexterity saving throw, taking 15 (6d4) piercing damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one. A creature has disadvantage on the saving throw if it is surprised. If it fails by 10 or more (DC 8), it is blinded until the end of the avatar's next turn. On each of the avatar's turns, the avatar may move the crows 50 feet in any direction (no action required). Using this ability does not reveal the avatar if it is hidden from a creature.
> 
> ### Bonus Actions
>
> ***Howl of the Great Beast (1/day).*** The avatar lets out a primeval howl. The avatar can designate any number of creatures it is aware of to be unaffected by it. Each affected creature within 120 feet of it that can hear it must make a DC 18 Wisdom saving throw. On a failed save, the creature drops whatever it is holding, loses concentration, and becomes frightened of the avatar. The creature can't take reactions and must take the Dash action to move away from the avatar by the safest available route on each of its turns, unless there is nowhere to move. At the end of its turn, the creature repeats the Wisdom save, ending the effect on it on a success.
>
> ***Bestial Take Down.*** The avatar makes one weapon attack. After the attack, the avatar falls prone. If it has 90 or fewer hit points, the attack is made with advantage.

\pagebreakNum

### Avatar of Beasts Tactics
Avatars of Beasts are ambush predators and experts at stealthily navigating woodland environments to attack from optimal hidden positions. Knocking enemies prone will be their primary tactic throughout the fight as it allows them to stack successive talon attacks on a single target more easily. The avatar never flees from combat unless directed to by someone controlling it.

#### Special Abilities

&emsp;**Flock of Doom.** The avatar generally uses this ability at the start of the fight, ideally before it's even spotted by the players. The avatar will stay hidden for as long as possible while withering away the players with the flock. The avatar will only charge into combat if it manages to blind a vulnerable player it can reach, or one of the players spot it. While the flock is active during combat, the avatar will position it to hinder ranged attackers. 

**Amber Breath.** This ability is deployed when the avatar can hit three or more targets simultaneously. 

#### Attack Sequence

The avatar's primary targets are those blinded by its flock and any vulnerable prey it can reach. The target's distance and whether it's prone affects how the avatar will attack.<br><br>

**Targets Within 60ft. & Howl of The Great Beast is Available.** 
* The avatar uses Howl of the Great Beast.
* It then closes the distance and makes a Gore attack, repositioning itself to get the bonus from Crashing Charge if necessary so it can attempt to knock its target prone. 
* If finishes with a stomp attack.

**Targets Within 60ft. & Howl of The Great Beast is Not Available.** 
* The avatar uses its Bestial Takedown bonus action to make a Gore attack, repositioning itself to get the bonus from Crashing Charge if necessary so it can attempt to knock its target prone. 
* If it manages to knock the target prone, it will follow up with two stomp attacks; otherwise, it will make two talon attacks.

**Targets Beyond 60ft.**
* The avatar dashes to its target.
* The avatar uses the Bestial Take Down bonus action to make a gore attack.
* The avatar stands back up.
Note, if the avatar lacks the remaining movement to stand back up, it will be unlikely to use Bestial Takedown and leave itself vulnerable.

**Targets Already Prone.**
* The avatar attacks with two talon attacks.
* If both attacks hit, it will follow up with a Bestial Takedown bonus action to make another talon attack.
* If any of the attacks miss, it will follow up with a Bestial Takedown bonus action to make a stomp attack.

\columnbreak

### Avatar of Beasts Adventures
The following table provides some ways to create adventures featuring these primal monsters in your games:

##### Avatar of Beasts Adventure Hooks

| d6  | Adventure Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Awakened Fury:** Recent logging activity in a revered forest has awakened an avatar of beasts. The avatar has started attacking nearby settlements, and the players must find a way to either appease it or confront it directly.|
|  2  | **Lost Ritual**: An ancient tablet describes the ritual to summon an avatar of beasts. Various factions are in a race to obtain and decipher the tablet, with the intention of harnessing the avatar's power for their own purposes.|
|  3  |**The Woodland Cult:** A cult of wilderness mystics plans to summon an avatar of beasts to cleanse the land of civilization. The players must find their ancient woodland shrine and disperse the cult before they can unleash the monster on the world. |
|  4  | **Bane of the Festival:** During a grand harvest festival, an old enemy of the town uses forbidden rituals to summon an avatar of beasts as an act of revenge. The festivities turn to chaos, with the players at the forefront of the defense. |
|  5  | **Bestial Pursuit:** While on a hunting expedition in a vast wilderness, the players disturb sacred grounds, and an avatar of beasts is summoned to repel the intruders. The players must navigate treacherous terrains while being stalked by the relentless elemental. |
|  6  | **Conduit of Rage:** A corrupted druid has found a way to channel their anger and hatred through an avatar of beasts, directing it to attack their enemies. The players, having crossed paths with the druid, find themselves in the avatar's path.|

### Avatar of Beasts Loot
Because these creatures are elementals, they don't have flesh and blood like mundane other creatures, and most of their body disintegrates when they die. Amidst the smokey ashes they leave behind, players may be able to salvage some bone or hide that remained corporeal or even some of their magical essence before it evaporates. This harvesting can usually be done using an **Intelligence (Arcana)** or **Wisdom (Nature)** check. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Avatar of Beasts Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.


##### Avatar of Beasts Loot Table
| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-10  | 1 500gp Item |
|  11-15 | 1d4(2) 500gp Items | 
|  16-21 | 1d4(2) 1,000gp Items  |  
|  22-25 |  1d6(3) 1,000gp Items |  
|  25+ |  1d4(2) 2,000gp Items |

## The Brass Bull

The Brass Bull was once a formidable chieftain of a <br> powerful minotaur tribe, feared and respected by his kin. His reign took a dark turn when, in a fit of insatiable hunger and rage, he devoured the tribe's bray speaker shaman, a sacred figure who communed with their dark gods. This sacrilegious act incurred the wrath of the gods, who sent a host of demons to punish him for his blasphemy. However, in a display of unparalleled ferocity and strength, the Brass Bull consumed the very demons sent to destroy him.

As punishment for this defiance, the demons cursed him with a bloodthirsty madness, transforming him into a relentless slaughtering machine. The Brass Bull rampaged across the land, driven by an unending desire to kill, his sanity consumed by the curse. He would have continued his rampage until death from exhaustion, but the dark gods, intrigued by his indomitable will and savage power, intervened once more. They remade him with metallic flesh, rendering him immune to fatigue and making him an eternal engine of destruction.

Now, the Brass Bull burns with an infernal heat, his metallic body glowing with an unholy fire as he leads his clan on a never-ending rampage. His presence on the battlefield is a harbinger of doom, his unstoppable fury leaving a trail of carnage in his wake. His metallic hide is nearly impenetrable, a testament to the dark gods' craftsmanship. However, a single weak point exists—a spot that glows with a reddish heat where the metal is weakest. Those who dare to challenge the Brass Bull must strike this precise point to bring him down, a near-impossible feat given his ferocity and the chaos that surrounds him in battle. 

\columnbreak


<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

##### Brass Bull Adventure Hooks

| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Fiery Siege:** A fortified city lies in the path of The Brass Bull's rampage. The players are hired to bolster the city's defenses, train its militia, and prepare for the inevitable assault. |
|  2  | **The Tortured Battlefield:** The site of one of The Brass Bull’s bloodiest massacres has become a haunted battlefield, filled with restless spirits. The players must cleanse the battlefield and use the information they gather to plan their assault on The Brass Bull. |
|  3  | **The Brass Secret:** A legendary blacksmith knows the secret to piercing The Brass Bull's hide. The players must protect the blacksmith from beastmen, gather rare materials for a special weapon, and then use this weapon to exploit The Brass Bull's weak point.
|  3  |**The Shaman's Vengeance:** The spirit of the bray speaker shaman originally devoured by The Brass Bull seeks revenge and reaches out to the players for assistance, offering them the power needed to slay the beast.

___

> ## The Brass Bull
> *Huge monstrosity (beastman), chaotic evil*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 20 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 299 (26d10+156)
> - **Speed** 40 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|22 (+6)|11 (+0)|22 (+6)|6 (-2)|20 (+5)|14 (+2)|
>___
> - **Saving Throws** Str +12, Dex +6, Int +4, Cha +8, Wis +11
> - **Damage Resistances** all damage
> - **Damage Immunities** fire, bludgeoning, piercing, and slashing from nonmagical attacks
> - **Condition Immunities** charmed, exhaustion, frightened
> - **Skills** Athletics +12, Perception +17, Intimidation +14, Stealth +6, Survival +17
> - **Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 27
> - **Languages** Abyssal
> - **Challenge** 18 (20,000 XP) &emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +6
> ___
>
> ***Labyrinthine Recall.*** The Brass Bull can perfectly recall any path it has traveled.
>
> ***Land's Stride.*** Moving through nonmagical difficult terrain does not cost the Brass Bull extra movement.
>
> ***Weak Point.*** Whenever a creature has advantage on an attack roll against the Brass Bull, it can choose to roll only one die instead of two as it aims for the Brass Bull's weak point. If the attack hits, the Brass Bull has vulnerability to the damage from the attack. The attack still counts as having advantage for the purposes of other abilities such as a rogue's Sneak Attack. If any damage would reduce the Brass Bull to 0 hit points that did not target its weak point, it is reduced to 1 hit point instead. The Brass Bull only dies if reduced to 0 hit points from damage dealt to its weak point.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The Brass Bull uses its Dread Presence and makes two attacks with its Rune-Tortured Axe.
>
> ***Charge.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +12 to hit, reach 5 ft., one creature. *Hit:* The target takes an extra 4 (1d8) piercing damage for each 10 feet the Brass Bull moved in a straight line before the attack.
>
> ***Crushing Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +12 to hit, reach 5 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 18 (3d8 + 6) piercing damage, the target takes an extra 4 (1d8) piercing damage for each 10 feet the Brass Bull moved in a straight line before the attack. If the target is a creature, it must succeed on a DC 20 Strength saving throw or be pushed up to 10 feet away and knocked prone. If the target fails by 10 or more, the creature is dazed* until the end of its next turn.
>
> ***Dread Presence.*** Each creature of the Brass Bull's choice that is within 120 feet of it and aware of it must succeed on a DC 18 Wisdom saving throw or become frightened for 1 minute. While frightened, the creature can't cast spells other than cantrips. A creature can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself on a success. If a creature's saving throw is successful or the effect ends for it, the creature is immune to the Brass Bull's Dread Presence for the next 24 hours.
>
> ***Rune-Tortured Axe.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +12 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 19 (3d8 + 6) slashing damage, plus 3 (1d6) fire damage for each level of rampage the Brass Bull has.
>
> ### Legendary Actions
> The Brass Bull can take 3 legendary actions, choosing from the options below. Only one legendary action option can be used at a time and only at the end of another creature's turn. The Brass Bull regains spent legendary actions at the start of its turn.
>
> **Check.** The Brass Bull makes a skill check that would normally require an action.
>
> **Blood Call.** The Brass Bull chooses a creature that just took its turn, which it can see within 120 feet of it, calling it into battle by having the creature's own blood turn on it. At the start of the creature's next turn, the target may move on its turn toward the Brass Bull by the most direct route, trying to get within 10 feet of it. The creature can then take the rest of its turn as normal, except it can't move away from the Brass Bull willingly and can't teleport. If it doesn't choose to move this way, it takes 22 (4d10) force damage.
>
> **Building Fury.** The Brass Bull moves up to half its movement then makes a Rune-Tortured Axe attack against a creature that just took its turn. If the attack hits and deals damage, the Brass Bull gains a level of rampage, up to a maximum of ten levels. Each level increases the Brass Bull's speed by 5 feet. All levels of rampage are lost after one minute of not gaining a level.
>
> **Tenacious Will.** If the Brass Bull is suffering from an effect that allows it to make a saving throw at the beginning or end of its turn, it may immediately make that saving throw with advantage. It can use this legendary action even while incapacitated.
>
> **Vent Heat (Costs 2 Actions).** The Brass Bull burns the air around it, forcing each creature within 10 feet of it to make a DC 18 Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 18 (4d8) fire damage and has disadvantage on the next attack roll it makes before the end of its next turn. On a successful save, a creature takes half as much damage and does not suffer disadvantage on its next attack.
>
> ### Reaction
>
> ***Block.*** The Brass Bull adds +6 to its AC against one attack that would hit it. To use this reaction, the Brass Bull must see the attacker and be wielding a melee weapon.
>
> **New condition described on next page*

\pagebreakNum

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

> ##### New Condition: Dazed 
> A dazed creature can’t take reactions and on its turn, it must choose whether it gets a move, an action, or a bonus action; it gets only one of the three.

### Epic Battle: Cataclysmic Onslaught
If you wish to turn the Brass Bull into an endgame threat, increase his Hit Points to 600 and give him the Cataclysmic Onslaught ability described below. These changes increase his Challenge Rating (CR) to 23.

### Cataclysmic Onslaught

When the Brass Bull rolls initiative, he can activate his Cataclysmic Onslaught. On initiative count 1 of each round during combat, he gains a new ability for the next minute on each following turn:

#### 1st Turn: Horrific Onslaught

The Brass Bull has advantage on attack rolls against creatures that are frightened of him.

#### 2nd Turn: Eldritch Onslaught

At the start of his turn, the Brass Bull chooses one creature within 150 feet of him that he is aware of. The chosen creature is engulfed in an agonizing inferno, taking 10 (3d6) fire damage and is set on fire for one minute. The burning target sheds bright light in a 30-foot radius and dim light for an additional 30 feet. The target cannot benefit from being invisible and has disadvantage on attack rolls. A creature can use its action to douse the fire by making a DC 16 Dexterity check. The flames are also extinguished if the creature is fully submerged in water or standing in an area with strong wind (at least 20 miles per hour). At the end of each of its turns while on fire, the creature takes 10 (3d6) fire damage, and the Brass Bull gains a level of rampage.

#### 3rd Turn: Unyielding Onslaught

Spells and other magical effects can neither reduce his speed nor cause him to be paralyzed or restrained, and he can spend 5 feet of movement to automatically escape from nonmagical restraints, such as manacles or a creature that has him grappled. Additionally, being underwater imposes no penalties on his movement or attacks.

#### 4th Turn: Bloodthirsty Onslaught

The Brass Bull has advantage on melee attack rolls against any creature that does not have all its hit points.

\columnbreak

### The Brass Bull's Lair
The Brass Bull does not maintain a traditional lair or remain in one location for an extended period. Instead, he roams the land, selecting locations to wreak havoc upon—often choosing relatively isolated villages or farmlands near woods for his temporary lairs. From these bases, he methodically spreads terror among the nearby inhabitants.

When fighting within his lair, the Brass Bull's Challenge Rating (CR) increases by 1.

#### Lair Actions
When the Brass Bull rolls initiative, his lair awakens to aid him, and until combat ends or the Brass Bull dies, the lair has an Intelligence 6 and can act of its own accord but always acts in the Brass Bull's best interest. While active this way, the lair is aware of the location of any creatures within it. On initiative count 20 (losing initiative ties), the lair can cause one of the following effects; it can't use the same effect two rounds in a row:

**Tide of Blood.** A wave of blood crashes down on an area within the lair, up to 30 feet long, 10 feet wide, and 10 feet tall. Each creature in that area must make a Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 13 (3d8) bludgeoning damage and is knocked prone. On a successful save, a creature takes half as much damage and isn’t knocked prone. If the Brass Bull is within the area of the wave, he takes no damage and instead regains 13 (3d8) hit points. If the wave passes through the space of three or more creatures, the Brass Bull gains a level of rampage.

**Seeping Wounds.** Wounded creatures within the lair begin to bleed profusely. Each creature with half or less of its hit points must make a DC 18 Constitution saving throw. Creatures at 0 hit points automatically fail this saving throw. On a failure, a creature takes 10 (3d6) necrotic damage. If two or more creatures fail this saving throw, the Brass Bull gains a level of rampage.

#### Regional Effects
The presence of the Brass Bull drastically affects his surroundings, bringing ruin and bloodshed that warp the land within 5 miles of his lair:

* Rivers in the area run red with blood.
* Corpses and other remains are preserved from decay and cannot become undead.
* Non-minotaur creatures within the area require three times the usual amount of rations per day. Additionally, any creature can consume raw meat without risk of sickness.
* Minotaurs in the area gain advantage on Wisdom (Perception) and Wisdom (Survival) checks to track or smell creatures that have lost more than half their hit points.

These effects gradually dissipate over 1d10 days after the Brass Bull's death.

### The Brass Bull Tactics

#### General Tactics
* **Dealing With Weak Point:** Prioritizes targets that consistently hit him with advantage, especially those resistant to his Dread Presence.
* **Block Reaction:** Reserves his reaction for the Block ability, using it against the attack likely to inflict the most damage.

#### Legendary Actions Usage
* **Building Fury:** Focuses on accumulating stacks of rampage whenever possible.
* **Blood Call:** Summons distant enemies closer for melee engagement.
* **Vent Heat:** Used when three or more targets can be hit simultaneously.

#### Cataclysmic Onslaught Tactics
* **1st Turn (Horrific Onslaught):** Targets those frightened by its dread presence to maximize rampage benefits, deviating from usual targets.
* **2nd Turn (Eldritch Onslaught):** Targets the creature furthest from its allies, limiting their ability to assist.
* **3rd Turn and Beyond:** Continues usual tactics, unaffected by the specific abilities used in previous onslaught turns.


### The Brass Bull Loot
Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from the Brass Bull consist of what can be harvested from his demonically blessed form. Because his hide and flesh are metallic in nature, it's up to you what qualities you want to assign it and how the players harvest it. For example, you could have players make an **Intelligence (Smith's Tools)** or **Intelligence (Leatherworker's Tools)** to collect his hide. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

You may also opt to simply have the players collect weapons and equipment he was carrying or wearing.

#### The Brass Bull Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.


##### The Brass Bull Loot Table

|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-9  | 2d4(5) 500gp Item |
|  10-12 | 1d6(3) 1,000gp Item | 
|  13-19 | 2d4(5) 1,000gp Items  |  
|  20-24 | 2d4(5) 1,000gp Items |  
|  25+ |  2d6(7) 2,000gp Items |

## Bray Speakers


Beastman bray speakers occupy a <br> mystical and revered position within the <br> beastmen society, serving as the conduit between <br> the physical world and the dark, chaotic realms of their deities. Adorned with gnarled staves and a collection of arcane charms, icons, and fetishes - many of which are intricately woven into their fur - bray speakers present an eerie and formidable presence. 

As the primary spellcasters among the beastmen, bray speakers bear the responsibility of divining the will of their dark gods. They are deeply attuned to the chaotic energies that permeate their lands and use this connection to interpret signs and omens. This role places them at the center of the beastmen's ceremonies, often leading dark rituals that range from desecrating the forests to performing blood sacrifices of captives. These ceremonies are crucial in calling forth the herds from the depths of the forest, rallying them for war, or appeasing their savage gods.

The bray speakers are also the custodians of the sacred monoliths scattered throughout the forest. These ancient stones serve as focal points for the beastmen's mystical energies and are the sites of many of their most significant rituals. The power emanating from these monoliths is harnessed by the speakers to conduct powerful rites, strengthen their connection to the dark gods, and imbue their followers with otherworldly might.

In the hierarchical society of the beastmen, bray speakers often act as advisors and guides to chieftains and other leaders. Their insights are considered invaluable, ensuring that the strategies and plans of the herd align with the perceived desires of their gods. 

This role imbues them with considerable influence, often placing them at the right hand of the most powerful leaders. They are among the only beastmen that need not fear attacks or challenges from others of their kind, for none would dare to harm a conduit of the gods.

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

> ##### New Condition: Emboldened  
> This document references the Emboldened condition. 
> * The Emboldened condition always lasts one minute.
> * An Emboldened creature deals additional 7 (2d6) damage when it hits with a attack.
> * At the end of the creature's turn, the Emboldened condition ends early if it missed with all of its attacks that turn, it is charmed or frightened, or is effected by *calm emotions* spell. 
> 

<br>

Bray speakers in beastmen society exhibit an array of magical abilities, each specializing in different arcane lores that reflect their connection to the natural and supernatural realms. Those attuned to the Lore of the Wilds channel the raw, malevolent forces of nature, manipulating the elements to unleash devastating spells that work to undo civility in all its forms. 

Speakers versed in the Lore of Beasts have a deep affinity with animals, able to summon and control various creatures or bestow their herds with beast-like ferocity and strength. The practitioners of the Lore of Death delve into the morbid and necrotic, wielding spells that sap life, summon spirits, and spread decay, embodying the finality of all life. Lastly, those who master the Lore of Shadows are adept in manipulation and illusion, using their magic to cloak their movements, sow confusion among enemies, and strike from where they are least expected. 

<img
src='https://draftsim.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/12/Ragemonger-Illustration-by-Karl-Kopinski.jpg'
style='position:absolute;top:-10px;right:-20px;width:850px;transform: scaleX(-1)' />

<img 
  src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;left:-200px;bottom:-675px;transform:rotate(200deg)' />

<img 
  src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;left:-200px;bottom:-780px;transform:rotate(180deg)' />

\pagebreakNum

Bray speakers within beastmen society vary in power, from lesser speakers associated with small herds to great speakers who counsel the most powerful leaders. Lesser speakers focus on minor rituals and guidance for smaller groups, honing their skills and gaining knowledge as they aspire to greater influence. In contrast, great speakers, at the pinnacle of this hierarchy, possess profound connections to the dark gods. They play crucial roles in strategic decisions, oversee major rituals, and channel significantly more potent magic.  These revered speakers are integral to the planning of large-scale operations, with their insights viewed as divine mandates, commanding deep respect and fear from their kin.

In battle, bray speakers are formidable opponents, using their dark magic to both bolster their allies and wreak havoc upon their enemies. Their spellcasting is instinctual and deeply entwined with the primal fury of their race. Drawing on the raw energies of their primeval homes and the chaotic power of their gods, they can unleash devastating spells, sow confusion among enemy ranks, and invigorate their beastmen brethren. This combination of mystical prowess and savage instinct makes the bray speakers a fearsome force, embodying the untamed and unpredictable essence of the malevolent wilds.

\columnbreak

> ### Traits
> ***Land's Stride.*** Moving through nonmagical difficult terrain does not cost the speaker extra movement.  
>
> ***Lore of Magic.*** The speaker is specialized in one of the following lores of magic: Beasts, Death, Shadow, or Wild. The chosen lore determines one of its traits and the spells it knows.  
>
> ***Primal Fury (Recharges after a short or long rest).*** When the speaker starts combat, it becomes Emboldened*.  
>
> ### Actions
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 6 (1d8 + 2) Piercing damage. If the speaker moved 20 feet or more straight toward the target immediately before the hit, the target must make a *Strength Saving Throw:* DC 12.<br> 
> *Failure:* The target is knocked Prone.  
>
> ***Quarterstaff.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 5 (1d6 + 2) Bludgeoning damage, or 6 (1d8 + 2) bludgeoning damage if wielded with two hands.  
>
> ***Spellcasting.*** The speaker is a spellcaster. Its spellcasting ability is Wisdom (spell save DC 13, +5 to hit with spell attacks). The spells the speaker knows depend on the lore of magic it has specialized in, as described in its **Lore of Magic** trait.
> 
>
> ### Bonus Actions
> ***Primal Magic.*** When the speaker takes the Attack action while Emboldened*, it can cast a spell this turn with a casting time of one action. 
>

### Lesser Bray Speaker <Br> Lore of Magic Options 
Select one of the following lores or magic to determine a lesser bray speaker's additional passive trait and spell list. <Br>
**New Spells Found In New Spells Section*<Br>
***Spell found in* The Xanathar's Guide to Everything

> #### Lesser Bray Speaker: Lore of Beasts
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Wild Heart.*** Whenever the speaker targets only itself or beast, monstrosity, giant, dragon, or fey with an Intelligence of 8 or less with a spell that requires concentration, it can choose for the spell to no longer require concentration. The spell ends early if the speaker is incapacitated or uses this feature to alter another spell. <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *druidcraft*, *primal savagery***<br>
> **1/Day:** *amber spear**, *heroism*, *mystic signal**, *pass without trace*

> #### Lesser Bray Speaker: Lore of Death
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Life Leech.*** Whenever a non-undead, non-construct creature fails a saving throw against or is hit by a spell attack from one of the speaker's spells of 1st level or higher, the speaker gets a +1 to its spell save DC and spell attack rolls for the next minute. It can only gain this bonus once per casting of a spell, and this bonus can stack up to 3 times (+3). <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *druidcraft*, *toll of the dead***<br>
> **1/Day:**  *aspect of dread**, *crippling pain**, *inflict wounds*, *mystic signal**

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br>

> #### Lesser Bray Speaker: Lore of Shadow
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Shadow Paths.*** When the speaker casts a spell of 1st level or higher, it may use teleportation to swap places with a willing Small, Medium, or Large creature within 30 feet of it that it can see.  <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *creeping strike**, *druidcraft* <br>
> **1/Day:** *mystic signal**, *mystifying miasma** *shroud of dusk**, *unseen lurker**

<br>

> #### Lesser Bray Speaker: Lore of The Wild
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Bestial Surge.*** When the speaker casts a spell of 4th level or lower that requires concentration while it is Emboldened, it can choose for the spell to no longer require concentration and instead tie the spell to the Emboldened condition. When the speaker is no longer Emboldened, the spell ends as if concentration has been broken.  <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *druidcraft*, *infestation***<br>
> **1/Day:** *devolve**, *mystic signal**, *primal scream**, *vile tide**

### Great Bray Speaker <Br> Lore of Magic Options 
Select one of the following lores or magic to determine <br> a great bray speaker's additional passive trait and spell list. <Br>
**New Spells Found In New Spells Section*
<Br>
***Spell found in* The Xanathar's Guide to Everything

> #### Great Bray Speaker: Lore of Beasts
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Wild Heart.*** Whenever the speaker targets only itself or one beast, monstrosity, giant, dragon, or fey with an Intelligence of 8 or less with a spell that requires concentration, it can choose for the spell to no longer require concentration. The spell ends early if the speaker is incapacitated or uses this feature to alter another spell. <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *druidcraft*, *primal savagery*** (3d10)<br>
> **1/Day:** *amber spear**, *aspect of the beast**, *find the path*, *heroism* (3rd level), *monstrous transformation**, *mystic signal**, *pass without trace*  


> #### Great Bray Speaker: Lore of Death
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Life Leech.*** Whenever a non-undead, non-construct creature fails a saving throw against or is hit by a spell attack from one of the speaker's spells of 1st level or higher, the speaker gets a +1 to its spell save DC and spell attack rolls for the next minute. It can only gain this bonus once per casting of a spell, and this bonus can stack up to 3 times (+3). <br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *druidcraft*, *toll of the dead*** (3d8)<br>
> **1/Day:** *aspect of dread**, *circle of death* (7th level), *crippling pain**, *find the path*, *impending doom**, *inflict wounds* (3rd level), *mystic signal**  

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

> #### Great Bray Speaker: Lore of Shadow
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Shadow Paths.*** When the speaker casts a spell of 1st level or higher, it may use teleportation to swap places with a willing Small, Medium, or Large creature within 30 feet of it that it can see.
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *creeping strike** (3d8), *druidcraft* <br>
> **1/Day:** *arcane signal**, *find the path*, *mystifying miasma**, *penumbral pendulum**, *pit of shadows** (7th level), *shroud of dusk** (3rd level), *unseen lurker**


> #### Great Bray Speaker: Lore of The Wild
>
> ##### **Trait:**
> ***Bestial Surge.*** When the speaker casts a spell of 4th level or lower that requires concentration while it is Emboldened, it can choose for the spell to no longer require concentration and instead tie the spell to the Emboldened condition. When the speaker is no longer Emboldened, the spell ends as if concentration has been broken.<br><br>
>
> ##### **Spell List:**
> **At will:** *druidcraft*, *infestation*** (3d6)<br>
> **1/Day:** *devolve** (3rd level), *find the path*, *mystic signal**, *mad rampage**, *primal scream**, *savage dominion**, *vile tide**

##### Bray Speaker Adventure Hooks

| d8  | Adventure Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Twisted Glade:** The players learn of a bray speaker conducting sinister rituals in a once-sacred glade, now shrouded in darkness. Venturing into the glade, they must disrupt the ritual, face the corrupted creatures summoned by the speaker, and restore the glade's purity before its darkness spreads to nearby lands.|
|  2  | **The Darkened Hills:** A series of hills have become a no-man’s-land, overrun by a beastman herd led by one or more bray speakers. Strange, malevolent energies are emanating from the hills, affecting the surrounding land. The players must investigate these energies, confront the speakers and their herd, and uncover the source of the growing darkness.|
|  3  |**The Shadowed Moon:** A series of lunar eclipses have been linked to a bray speaker wielding the Lore of Shadows. The players are tasked to track down and confront the speaker before he completes a ritual that could plunge the region into perpetual darkness, dealing with both his deceptive magics and beastmen guardians. |
|  4  | **The Beast Hunter:** A bray speaker, adept in the Lore of Beasts, has unleashed ferocious magical beasts to hunt down specific targets. The players must protect the next target, a local dignitary or a member of their own group, and find a way to counter the speaker's control over these beasts. |
|  5  | **Reach of the Wilds:** A forest has begun to encroach upon nearby settlements, driven by a bray speaker wielding the Lore of the Wilds. The players must venture into the hostile forest, face the speaker's wild elemental spells, and find a way to halt the forest's unnatural growth. |
|  6  | **The Deathly Blight:** Crops are failing and livestock are dying in a rural area, believed to be the work of a bray speaker wielding the Lore of Death. The players are hired to end the blight, requiring them to confront the speaker and his deathly minions, and possibly find a way to reverse the damage done to the land.|
|  7  | **The Herdstone Ritual:** People from nearby villages and farmsteads are being snatched away into the forest each night by beastmen serving a bray speaker preparing a wicked ritual at an eldritch monolith deep in the woods that will transform the captives into beastmen. The players must intervene and save the kidnapped victims before the rise of the full moon allows the speaker to complete his ritual.|
|  8  | **The Circle of Thorns:** A circle of bray speakers has convened in a deep forest to perform a ritual that threatens to unleash a wave of wild magic across the land. The players must navigate through treacherous woodlands, disrupt the gathering, and contend with the combined magical might of the speakers, each wielding a different arcane lore|


\columnbreak

### Bray Speaker Tactics

Bray speakers serve as the primary spellcasters of the beastmen war herds. Unlike most other spellcasters, they are fairly durable and can engage in melee combat while using their spells. With their Primal Fury active, bray speakers can cast spells while also making attacks. This makes them formidable foes as they don't suffer the vulnerabilities of most spellcasters and won't hesitate to dive into melee combat.

The following tactics assume the bray speaker is accompanied by at least two other beastmen.

The lore of magic a bray speaker is specialized in significantly influences its combat tactics. Below are tactics specific to the different lores and their spells:

#### Lore of Beasts

These bray speakers primarily serve a support role, which is helped by the fact that their Wild Heart trait works with most beastmen creatures.

##### Lore of Beasts Spells

**Pass Without Trace:** This ideally cast before combat begins. However, if allies can hide as a bonus action during combat, this spell remains useful during the fight.

**Amber Spear:** This should be cast when there's an opportunity to hit two or more targets.

**Aspect of the Beast:** This is typically cast on the speaker's most powerful ally. Ripping Jaws is generally the most useful for the Beastmen. With it, a beastman can use its Charge ability to topple a target and then bite with a higher chance of success. Additionally, the extra piercing damage from Primal Fury boosts the temporary hit points gained from the Ripping Jaws attack.

**Heroism:** This spell can be useful for either other beastmen or the speaker. It ensures the target isn't easily frightened, helping to mainain their Primal Fury. 

It's important to remember that this spell only benefits from the Wild Heart trait when cast at 1st level. For higher-level speakers, this often becomes their primary concentration spell.

**Monstrous Transformation:** This spell acts as a reset for the speaker. Upon transformation, the likelihood of reverting to their original form during combat is minimal. This spell is generally activated when the speaker's health drops below half or when it loses Primal Fury. While the transformed creature can't cast spells, any prior ongoing spells persist. 

Depending on the situation, the speaker might transform into a:

* **Manticore.** Preferable when adversaries have limited ranged capabilities

* **Hydra.** Chosen when foes have a lower damage output or can't focus their attacks on the transformed speaker

* **Dragon.** Optimal when opponents are grouped together, allowing the dragon's breath to hit multiple targets or when facing adversaries with high elemental damage output.

\pagebreakNum



#### Lore of Shadows
The Shadow Paths trait of this lore works well when combined with beastmen who have the Charge ability. By swapping places with units like besthorns or warhorns, the speaker can help them get in repeated charges during a fight.

##### Lore of Shadows Spells
**Pit of Shadows:** This spell is used at the earliest opportunity when it can affect two or more targets.

**Mystifying Miasma:** This is the speaker's go-to opening spell, unless *Pit of shadows* is available. It's used to disperse tightly packed enemy formations.

**Penumbral Pendulum:** This is employed when it can strike two or more foes. After casting it, the speaker's allies may attempt to grapple and restrain adversaries, ensuring they remain within the pendulum's path.

**Unseen Lurker:** This spell generally targets the speaker's strongest ally and is cast when no other spells take precedence or if the speaker requires an urgent retreat.

**Shroud of Dusk:** This spell is particularly handy during close-quarters combat. If the bray speaker knows it will have disadvantage on its next attack, this spell's darkness can level the playing field by canceling out any sources of advantage and disadvantage for most creatures in its area.

#### Lore of Death

Bray speakers practicing the Lore of Death tend to reserve their more potent spells for later rounds of combat, capitalizing on the enhanced power derived from their Leech Life ability.

##### Lore of Death Spells

**Circle of Death:** Given its vast area of effect, speakers prefer to cast this spell prior to engaging in melee combat, ensuring maximum enemy exposure.



**Aspect of Dread:** This spell is typically used after the speaker engages in melee combat. After charging in and making a Gore attack, the speaker will cast this spell while surrounded by foes to sow fear.



**Impending Doom:** This spell should target formidable enemy frontline fighters. This will help other beastmen knock them over with charging attacks.

**Inflict Wounds:** Speakers are patient with this spell, waiting for an opportune moment to strike a target when they have advantage.

**Crippling Pain:** This is best cast on agile skirmishers like monks or rogues. Its potency is amplified when targeting a prone adversary, as the act of standing further exacerbates the damage the target takes.


#### Lore of The Wild
Bray speakers dedicated to this lore tend to be less melee-focused, especially those with access to the Savage Domain spell. The majority of their spells require concentration, but their Bestial Surge trait allows them to maintain multiple spells at once, and they will often have at least one spell going that can help them disrupt the concentration of enemy spellcasters.


\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>



##### Lore of the Wild Spells

**Savage Dominion:** This spell is cast pre-combat unless doing so would jeopardize a surprise attack. While maintaining concentration on this spell, the speaker keeps its distance, remaining within 60 feet of the summoned monster. The type of summoned creature is typically random unless the speaker possesses prior knowledge about adversaries.

The choices are:

* **Giant:** Chosen if adversaries are adept at avoiding melee or are fighting at a distance

* **Jabberwocky:** Chosen when the objective is to hamper foes with the creature's Burble and other debilitating effects. (Remember that the Burble ability is indiscriminate, potentially affecting even the speaker if it gets too close.)

* **Behemoth:** A versatile monster, adept at singling out and consuming targets, as well as attacking groups with its Rend ability

**Mad Rampage:** This should be cast on a unit with multiple attacks. Great speakers might cast it on the creature summoned with *savage domain*.

**Vile Tide:** This should be used when it can target two or more opponents or disrupt a spell-concentrating foe, especially if *devolve* has already been used on them.

**Primal Scream:** This should be reserved for critical moments. It's typically cast on the speaker itself or on powerful allies like a warhorn or a creature summoned by *savage domain*. It's most effective when the targeted unit is at half-health and can affect at least two foes with the scream.

**Devolve:** This spell is saved for when the speaker can target an enemy spellcaster with it.

### Bray Speaker Loot
Because beastmen are humanoids, most of the <br> valuable goods that can be looted from them are <br> the remains of the equipment they were using or <br> valuables they were carrying, though it is common <br> to harvest horns from their fallen. Most dropped <br> valuables can be found using an **Intelligence <br> (Investigation)** check.

Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly  <br>using a flat modifier.


#### Bray Speaker Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items <br> and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results <br> of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting <br> or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

|  11-17 | 1d4(2) 5gp Items  |  
|  18-21 | 1 10gp Items |  
|  22+ |  1d4(2) 10gp Items |

## Beastman Infantry
The hierarchy of the beastmen is primarily determined by strength and brutality. The bulk of beastmen are known as longhorns and represent the typical members of their kind. Beneath them are the wretched shorthorns who represent the dregs of their society, and above them are the elite besthorns who lord over the rest of their kin. All these beastmen make up the infantry fighters of a beastmen force going to war and are typically lead by the most powerful among them. Warhorns lead smaller war herds or serve as secondary leaders in large war herds, which are typically led by the most powerful of all beastman warriors: the beastlords.

### Shorthorns
Shorthorns, the lowest caste among the beastmen, are a pitiful sight to behold in their dark, twisted society. These lesser beastmen are easily recognized by their diminutive, stunted horns, a physical manifestation of their lowly status within the brutal hierarchy of their kin. Their horns, small and often malformed, set them apart as the weakest and least respected of their race.

Physically, shorthorns possess a devilish appearance, with gaunt frames, sharp, angular features, and eyes that gleam with malice and cunning. Their snarling expressions reveal a nature twisted by resentment and cruelty. Despite their smaller stature and less imposing presence, there is something undeniably sinister about their demeanor, a reflection of the bitterness that festers in their hearts.



<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

This low status among their brethren imbues the shorthorns with a deep-seated cruelty. They are often treated with contempt and abuse by the larger, stronger beastmen, which in turn makes the shorthorns resentful and vindictive. Given the opportunity, they vent this malice with savage glee, particularly upon captured prisoners who fall into their clutches. 
Their treatment of such unfortunates is merciless and filled with inventive brutality, a means for them to exert power in the few ways they can.

Despite their low rank, shorthorns are essential to the functioning of a beastmen herd. They perform duties that others have no patience for or are too clumsy to handle, such as maintaining weapons and equipment. Their dexterous fingers are well-suited for intricate tasks, and they often find themselves tending to the arms and armor of their more formidable kin, a role that, while menial, is crucial for the warband's effectiveness.

In the chaos of battle, shorthorns are typically relegated to the role of expendable light infantry. Their weak and cowardly nature is well-known, and they are often sent to the front lines as cannon fodder. In the heat of combat, their lack of courage becomes apparent; they are quick to flee at the first sign of the tide turning against them. This behavior reinforces their status as the lowest of their kind, yet their numbers and willingness to swarm the enemy in droves can sometimes turn the tide in a skirmish, albeit at a great cost to their own ranks.

> ### Traits
> ***Bestial Ambush.*** The shorthorn gets +3 to initiative (14) and its speed increases by 20 feet on its first turn in combat if it was not Surprised.  
> 
> ***Land's Stride.*** Moving through nonmagical difficult terrain does not cost the shorthorn extra movement.  
> 
> ***Primal Fury (Recharges after a short or long rest).*** When the shorthorn starts combat, it becomes Emboldened*.  
> 
> ### Actions  
> 
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +3 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 3 (1d4 + 1) Piercing damage. If the shorthorn moved 20 feet or more straight toward the target, it must make a *Strength Saving Throw:* DC 11. <br>
*Failure:* The target is knocked Prone.   
> 
> ***Spear.*** *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack:* +3 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 20/60 ft., one target. *Hit:* 4 (1d6 + 1) Piercing damage.

#### Shorthorn Tormentors
Some shorthorns achieve a special level of notoriety, <br> earning them the title Tormentor. These shorthorns, renowned for their exceptional cruelty and proficiency <br> in torture, wield poisonous spears with chilling <br> expertise. Unlike their typical counterparts, tormentors <br> are feared and respected, not for brute strength, but for <br> their ability to inflict prolonged agony. Their spears, laced with lethal toxins from forest flora and fauna, are designed <br> to incapacitate and torture rather than kill swiftly. In battle, these weapons become instruments of terror, <br> foreshadowing the grim fate of those who fall into their clutches, and they take deviant glee in ganging up on vulnerable targets.

The tormentors' notoriety, however, is most pronounced <br> in their role as skilled torturers. Their gruesome methods are a perverse art form, earning them a unique, elevated status within the beastmen's brutal society. Beastmen chieftains often entrust them with the torture of particularly hated captives, a task they relish. This grim responsibility grants the Tormentors a level of respect and authority rarely afforded to other shorthorns.

The target can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on a success.  
>

>

#### Shorthorn Raiders

Shorthorn raiders occupy a unique and vital role within the ranks of the beastmen. As specialists in scouting and ranged combat, these shorthorns distinguish themselves through their proficiency with crudely made bows, a rarity in a culture that typically favors brute force and melee combat. Their skill with these weapons, combined with their natural agility and stealth, makes them ideal scouts and ranged support for the more brutish members of their kind. Shorthorn raiders are adept at moving silently through dense forests, their keen eyes and sharp senses constantly scanning for signs of the enemy or opportunities for ambush.

The intelligence gathered by these raiders is invaluable to the beastmen chieftains, enabling them to coordinate devastating ambushes and strike at prime targets with little to no warning. Their ability to relay critical information about enemy movements, weaknesses, and terrain plays a pivotal role in the beastmen's guerrilla warfare tactics. In the heat of battle, shorthorn raiders skulk on the fringes, loosing volleys of arrows into the enemy ranks, sowing chaos and confusion from a distance while their brethren engage in close-quarters bloodshed.

However, the ambitions of the shorthorn raiders often extend beyond mere reconnaissance. Emboldened by their mastery of stealth and archery, they sometimes undertake their own raids, pillaging and burning villages when they believe they can evade retribution. These raids are swift and brutal, characterized by a sudden onslaught of arrows followed by the merciless slaughter of any who survive the initial assault. 

\columnbreak

#### Shorthorn Stalkers

Shorthorn stalkers represent the pinnacle of skill and discipline among the shorthorn raiders, setting a standard for stealth and skirmishing tactics that few in the beastmen ranks can match. These elite raiders are renowned for their hit-and-run tactics, striking with precision and vanishing before the enemy can mount a proper defense. Their exceptional agility and mastery of the terrain allow them to navigate the densest forests and roughest terrains with ease, making them the perfect operatives for quick, devastating strikes. 

As scouts, the shorthorn stalkers are remarkably reliable and disciplined, a trait that is somewhat atypical in the often chaotic and impulsive beastmen society. They excel in reconnaissance, gathering crucial information about enemy positions, numbers, and movements with a level of efficiency that is invaluable to any beastman chieftain. Their reports are precise and timely, allowing for the swift planning of raids and ambushes. In the field, they act as the eyes and ears of the beastmen warbands, ensuring that their brute force is applied with strategic cunning and surprise, maximizing the impact of their attacks.

The role of the shorthorn stalkers in the beastmen hierarchy is unique. Despite their lowly origins, their skills and contributions are indispensable, earning them a place of unique value in the herd. They are the silent, deadly shadow of the beastmen hordes, often the difference between a successful raid and a disastrous engagement. 

\columnbreak

### Longhorns

Longhorns are the primary representation of a beastman, forming the backbone of their savage herds. They are a fearsome blend of animal and human. Their lower bodies boast powerful, goat-like, bipedal legs, adept for traversing rough, forested terrains with ease. Their human-like torsos and arms showcase grotesque but powerful muscles. Above this, their heads are akin to that of a fanged goat, complete with menacing horns. However, within their ranks, many variations of beastman can exist, exhibiting a mix of traits from different wild animals. This diversity adds to their terrifying presence, as each longhorn presents a unique yet uniformly intimidating appearance.

The longhorns make up the majority of the beastmen herds. Their numbers are vast, and they form the core of the beastmen's marauding forces. Characterized by their rowdy and impulsive nature, longhorns are creatures of instinct and aggression. They are quick to anger, and once provoked, their fury is relentless and brutal. This temperament, while often chaotic, is a significant asset in the heat of battle, as it fuels their ferocity and resilience. However, once they lose their momentum and their fury burns out, they can become less confident and unreliable fighters.

Longhorns are primarily melee combatants, relying on their natural speed and brute strength to overpower their foes. They typically lack discipline, and their equipment is often crudely made and poorly maintained, but what they lack in finesse, they more than make up for with sheer rage-fueled power. Their approach to battle is straightforward and savage: they charge headlong into enemy ranks, using their horns, teeth, and any weapon at hand to wreak havoc. This makes them excellent shock troops, capable of breaking enemy lines through sheer force and the intimidating might of their charge. Foes knocked prone by the charge of their horns are quickly dogpiled by other beastmen who relish the opportunity to prey on a newly vulnerable victim.

#### Longhorn Ravagers

Longhorn ravagers, a notorious subgroup within the beastman ranks, are as feared for their chaotic behavior as they are for their combat prowess. Known for their love of potent, rank brews, these ravagers are seldom seen without their signature flasks or containers of alcohol. This drink, foul to any but their own kind, serves as a source of inebriation and a form of battle stimulant. In the midst of combat, the intoxicating effects of their brew do more than impair; they invigorate the ravagers, fueling their already formidable aggression and bolstering their confidence. This alcohol-induced bravado often turns the tide of battle, as the ravagers, lost in their drunken fury, become even more fearsome and unpredictable adversaries.

The longhorn ravagers have also developed a unique fighting style that incorporates their drinking vessels. Whether it's a crude mug, a battered flask, or even an entire keg, these containers are not just for holding their brew but are also cleverly used as improvised shields. This unconventional approach to defense is surprisingly effective, allowing the ravagers to absorb blows that would fell lesser beastmen. 


\columnbreak

<br>

Despite their drunken demeanor, the destructive power of the longhorn ravagers should not be underestimated. Their alcohol-induced courage often leads them to hold their ground in the face of overwhelming odds, where other beastmen might break and flee. This tenacity, coupled with their wild, unpredictable nature, makes them unlikely elite warriors. In battle, the ravagers are the embodiment of chaotic strength, a whirlwind of fury and resilience, their roars of inebriated rage echoing as both a battle cry and a warning to all who face them.

<br>

> ##### Number of Swig Uses
> The default number of uses of the Swig represents the average amount of drink a longhorn is carrying with it at any given time. There may be a reason why a longhorn would have more or less drink on its person, and you can adjust the number of daily uses of the Swig ability to reflect this.

> ***Bestial Ambush.*** The longhorn gets +3 to initiative (15) and its speed increases by 20 feet on its first turn in combat if it was not Surprised.

> ***Land's Stride.*** Moving through nonmagical difficult terrain does not cost the longhorn extra movement.

>

*Failure:* The target is knocked Prone. 
> 
> ### Bonus Actions
> ***Swig (2/day).*** The longhorn takes a swig of its drink. If it does so, it takes 5 (2d4) poison damage, gains advantage on all melee weapon attacks during the turn, and attack rolls against it have advantage until the start of its next turn. It also ends any effect causing it to be Charmed or Frightened, and becomes Emboldened*.

### Besthorns
Besthorns stand at the pinnacle of the beastman hierarchy, representing the most elite and formidable warriors within their brutal society. These fearsome creatures bear a resemblance to their longhorn brethren, but they are distinguished by their grander, more majestic horns and more robust, powerful physiques. While they may be of the same stock as longhorns, besthorns view themselves as a class apart, seeing the longhorns as inferior and unworthy of comparison. 

Armed and armored with the finest spoils of war, Besthorns have access to the best equipment looted from countless raids. Their weapons are often of higher quality the herd can get their hands on, and their armor is more complete and protective than that of the average beastman. This access to superior gear is a privilege earned through their proven prowess in battle and their elevated status in the herd. The sight of a besthorn donned in heavy armor wielding a massive battle axe is both imposing and terrifying, a testament to their position as the apex predators of their society.

In terms of combat skill and discipline, besthorns are a step above the typical longhorn. They are more battle-hardened and tactically astute, capable of executing complex strategies and holding the line where others might falter. This discipline and martial prowess make them the preferred choice for the chieftain's personal retinue, serving as both elite guards and the most trusted warriors in the herd. Their presence in a chieftain's entourage is a clear sign of his strength and the respect he commands.

However, the ambition and strength of the besthorns often put them in a position to challenge for leadership. It is among their ranks that contenders for the title of chieftain most frequently arise. These challenges are brutal and decisive, for in the world of the beastmen, might makes right, and the strongest rule. The besthorns, with their superior abilities and equipment, are often the most likely to succeed in these contests, ensuring that the leadership of the herd remains in the hands of the most formidable and fearsome among them.

\columnbreak

#### Besthorn Manrippers
Besthorn manrippers are the embodiment of sheer brutality and skill within the already formidable ranks of the mesthorns. These elite warriors have honed their mastery of the massive greataxes, weapons that are as deadly as they are symbolic of their wielders' status and power. The manrippers have earned their fearsome title through countless battles, where they demonstrated an uncanny ability to cleave through multiple foes in a single, devastating swing. 

The greataxes wielded by the manrippers are not just tools of war; they are extensions of their own savage nature. Honed to be as lethal as possible, these axes are capable of delivering strikes that not only cut through armor and bone but can also bisect an opponent with terrifying ease. The manrippers have perfected the use of these axes to such a degree that what might be a survivable blow from another warrior becomes a deadly, maiming strike in their hands. Their ability to turn the tide of battle with a few well-placed swings makes them both valuable and feared assets in any beastman warband.

In the ranks of the beastmen, the besthorn manrippers are viewed with a mixture of jealous awe and cowering terror. Their presence on the battlefield is enough to demoralize enemies and inspire their fellow beastmen with their sheer ferocity and combat prowess. As they wade through enemy ranks, leaving a trail of destruction in their wake, the manrippers embody the apex of beastman martial ability. They are not just fighters; they are symbols of the raw, unbridled power and savagery that define the beastmen's way of war, making them a terrifying force to be reckoned with.


\columnbreak

### Beastmen Chieftains
Beastman chieftains stand as towering figures of power <br> and authority within the savage society of the beastmen. These formidable leaders have risen through the ranks,  often through sheer strength and brutality, to a position where they command entire herds. Their ascent to power is a testament to their prowess in battle and their ability to dominate and control their kin, traits revered among the beastmen. A chieftain is not just a leader; they are the epitome of what a beastman aspires to be - strong, commanding, and fearsome.

Filled with a supreme sense of confidence and superiority, beastman chieftains view themselves as above all other creatures. This arrogance is not unfounded, as their physical and martial capabilities often far exceed those of their subordinates. Their mere presence on the battlefield is a source of inspiration for other beastmen, bolstering their confidence and battle fury. The chieftain's roar of command or charge into battle can ignite the frenzied rage of their herd, transforming a disorganized mob into a focused, albeit still chaotic, fighting force. Under the leadership of a chieftain, the beastmen become more than just a rabble of savages; they become a terrifying wave of destruction.

Coordinating the chaotic and unruly nature of the beastmen herds is no small feat, and it is here that the chieftains truly demonstrate their leadership. They are the strategists and coordinators behind the beastmen's raids and battles, adept at deploying their forces against the most hated enemies of their kind. Often, a chieftain is advised by a speaker, a mystical figure who provides guidance on the spiritual and strategic aspects of their campaigns. This speaker advisor plays a crucial role in decision-making, offering insights on when and how to best utilize the beastmen under the chieftain's command so that they best fulfill the will of their dark gods. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

#### Warhorns

Warhorns are formidable figures within <br> their herds, having fought fiercely to attain <br> their dominant positions. Their rise to power <br> is a testament to their unmatched strength and combat prowess, setting them apart from the other ranks within the beastmen society. These leaders see themselves as superior, not just in terms of physical might but also in their ability to command and direct the actions of their herd. Their authority is undisputed, born from a brutal culture where strength and the ability to instill fear are the keys to leadership.

Unlike typical leaders who might engage in the intricacies of governance, warhorns are singularly focused on maintaining their authority and orchestrating the acts of raiding and warfare that define the beastmen's existence. They are less concerned with the day-to-day affairs of the herd, leaving the herd to squabble amongst themselves. Their primary concern lies in ensuring that their position of dominance remains unchallenged. This involves a balance of displaying ruthless strength to deter potential challengers and demonstrating enough strategic wisdom to lead successful raids and battles. The life of a warhorn is one of constant vigilance and aggression, as any sign of weakness could invite challenges from ambitious underlings.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/JxgQdjj/Ondu-Champion-Battle-for-Zendikar-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-0px; right:-340px; width:1200px; transform:scaleX(-1)' />

\pagebreakNum


#### Beastlords
Beastlords represent the apex of power and authority in the savage hierarchy of the beastmen. They are formidable figures, towering above even the mighty warhorns in terms of strength, leadership, and sheer presence. A beastlord's rule extends not just over a single herd but over multiple warherds, which they unite into a single, overwhelming force of destruction. Their ability to command and coordinate such a vast array of brutal warriors is a testament to their unparalleled dominance and strategic acumen. In the world of the beastmen, where might and ferocity are the cornerstones of power, the beastlords are the ultimate embodiment of these traits.

Under a beastlord's command, warhorns serve as lieutenants or subcommanders, each overseeing individual herds within the larger force. This structure allows the beastlord to exert control over a massive number of troops, delegating responsibilities to these trusted commanders while maintaining overall strategic direction. 

<br>

\columnbreak

<br><br>

The warhorns, in turn, respect and fear the beastlord, recognizing their superior strength and the privilege of serving under such a powerful leader. This hierarchy ensures that the beastlord's will is executed efficiently and ruthlessly across the multiple herds under their dominion.

To the other beastmen, a Beastlord is more than just a leader; he is seen as the living embodiment of the will of their dark gods. When a Beastlord unites the warherds for a campaign, he is perceived as a divine mandate, a signal that a great wave of destruction is about to be unleashed upon the civilized world. This belief imbues the beastmen with fanatical zeal, as they view their campaigns under a beastlord's command as sacred acts of war, destined to bring ruination and chaos in the name of their dark deities. The appearance of a beastlord at the head of a united beastmen force is a dire portent, heralding a time of strife and devastation for all who stand against them.

<br>

> ### Actions
> **Multiattack.** The warhorn makes two melee attacks.

> ***Javelin.*** *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack:* +7 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 120 ft., one target. *Hit:* 11 (2d6 + 4) Piercing damage.
> 
> ### Bonus Actions
> ***Unrelenting.*** If the warhorn misses with two attacks against the same target on the same turn, it may make a Gore attack against that target with advantage. 
>
> **New condition described at the end of the section*
