##### Beastmen Infantry Adventure Hooks
| d20  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Safeguarding Sanctity:** A local village enlists the adventurers' help after a sacred relic is stolen during a shorthorn raid. The relic must be retrieved before the shorthorns have the chance to take it back to their herd, where it can be defiled.|
|  2  |**Shorthorn Uprising:** The adventurers stumble upon an internal conflict within a beastman herd. An unusually large influx of shorthorns has destabilized the balance of power in the herd, leading the shorthorns to attempt an uprising against the bullying longhorns. Can the adventures use this upset to their advantage? |
|  3  |**Victim of Torment:** A prominent figure from a nearby town has been captured by a notorious gang of shorthorn tormentors. The adventurers are hired to rescue the captive before it's too late. |
|  4  |**The Raider's Plunder:** Shorthorn raiders have been attacking trade caravans, disrupting vital supply routes. The adventurers are hired to protect a particularly valuable caravan or to track down the raiders' hideout and put an end to their attacks.  |
|  5  | **The Shorthorn Scouts:** A village the party is visiting comes under attack by shorthorn raiders acting as reconnaissance for a larder war herd. If the players don't prevent the shorthorns' escape, they will alert the herd to the village's presence.|
|  6  | **The Stalkers' Gauntlet:** While traveling through the forest, the party finds themselves in a trap-filled woodland gauntlet set up by a group of shorthorn stalkers looking to prove themselves as elite hunters to their herd's chieftain.|
| 7  | **The Corrupted Grove:** A sacred grove has been corrupted by the presence of longhorns, who are using it as a base to launch raids on nearby settlements, and the players must cleanse the grove of the beastmen's taint. |
| 8  | **The Savaged Caravan:** A trade caravan has gone missing in an area known to be frequented by longhorn herds. The players are hired to track down the caravan and rescue any survivors.  |
| 9 | **Brewing Chaos:** A mysterious, potent brew has begun circulating in a nearby town, causing those who drink it to become violent and uncontrollable. The source of this brew is traced back to the Longhorn Ravagers, who are rallying for an attack on the town. The players must eliminate the ravagers and find out how the brew is being distributed throughout the town. |
|10 | **The Besthorns' Pact:** A series of brutal attacks by a group of besthorns on nearby villages leads to an unsettling discovery – they are not acting alone. They serve a more sinister force. The players must investigate the nature of this alliance, disrupt it, and face the combined might of the besthorns and their new masters.|

\columnbreak

|   |  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  11  | **The Iron Convoy:** A convoy carrying masterwork weapons and armor is scheduled to pass through a region where besthorns have been spotted. The players are tasked with escorting the convoy, ensuring the besthorns don't plunder it to upgrade their arsenal.|
|  12  |**The Bloodied Glade:** A sacred glade has been desecrated by the besthorn manrippers, who use it as a site for their brutal rites and trials of strength. A druidic circle enlists the players to cleanse and reclaim the glade |
|  13  |**War of Desecration:** A warhorn has declared a war of desecration, targeting a series of ancient, mystical sites for defilement. The players must protect these sites, each offering unique challenges and guardians, and ultimately confront the warhorn.|
|  14  |**The Beastman Bounty:** A wealthy noble offers a substantial bounty for the head of a notorious warhorn who has been raiding his lands. The players embark on a dangerous hunt, but as they delve deeper, they uncover unsettling truths about the noble's past dealings with the beastmen.  |
|  15  | **The Beastlord's Conquest:** A powerful beastlord has begun uniting the disparate beastmen tribes, posing a massive threat to the region. The players are hired by a coalition of local rulers to either assassinate the beastlord or sow discord among the united tribes to break up the growing beastmen coalition before it can launch a full-scale invasion.|
|  16  | **The Beastlord's Prize:** An ancient artifact of great power has been discovered by a beastlord. The players are recruited by a secret society that seeks to prevent the artifact from being used for destructive purposes. They must track down the beastlord's encampment, retrieve the artifact, and navigate through the ensuing chaos as the beastmen realize their prize is being stolen.|
| 17  |**The Besieged Inn.** The party visits an inn where refugees from the surrounding countryside are fortifying themselves for the night as they prepare to fend off the inevitable attacks from the beastmen raiders who drove them here.|
| 18  | **The Beastpath Crossing.** The party stumbles upon an intersection of woodland paths used by the beastmen and soon find themselves facing attacks from multiple directions by incoming beastman soldiers.  |
|19 | **Ruinous Beasts:** An expedition to explore ancient ruins goes missing in a region known for beastman activity. The players must rescue the survivors, if any, and face the beastman forces that lurk within the ruins, unraveling the secrets of a long-lost civilization and its connection to the beastmen.|
| 20 | **The Dark Forest Beckons:** A dense forest known to be a beastman stronghold begins to expand mysteriously, encroaching upon nearby settlements. The players are tasked with investigating the cause of this unnatural growth, leading them to confront the beastman forces within and uncovering an ancient power that the beastmen seek to harness. |


\pagebreakNum

### Beastmen Infantry Tactics
The beastmen are hard-hitting ambushers. They aren't as effective if they can't catch their foes by surprise or are stuck in a prolonged fight. Nonetheless, their recklessly aggressive nature and intense disdain for civilization will often drive them into fights where they may not have the best tactical advantages. 

There are a few abilities common to all beastmen infantry.

**Bestial Ambush.** This ability's primary purpose is to give beastmen an offensive edge when they first engage with players. However, it doesn't always need to be used in the first round of combat. Some stealthier beastmen can wait until they've snuck up on a better target before making their first attack and triggering the ability.

**Charge & Gore.** While every beastman can use their Charge ability to knock a foe prone, most can't capitalize on the advantage it grants them due to not having multiattack. Therefore, it works best to have multiple beastmen gang up on a single target so others can make follow-up attacks on prone targets.

**Primal Fury.** Beastmen will never flee while this ability is active. This ability underscores the importance of ensuring beastmen do whatever they can to help their attacks hit. This most commonly includes attacking surprised or prone enemies.

#### Shorthorn Tactics
These beastmen are weak and cowardly by nature and will usually only press an attack if they feel they have an advantage that tips the odds in their favor. This advantage could range from a surprise attack to overwhelming numbers or the use of forested terrain to launch hit-and-run attacks. Once they feel they're on the winning side, shorthorns will charge in with the same reckless ferocity common to most beastmen.

##### Shorthorn Tormentors
These beastmen typically move ahead of the rest of their warband, setting up ambushes that their allies can capitalize on. If they can pull off the ambush, they'll use their poisonous attacks to weaken players and leave them more susceptible to the charges of other beastmen. Once an enemy is prone, the tormentors will surround it and ensure it can't get back up. These tactics make tormentors ideal allies for stronger beastmen like longhorns and besthorns.

##### Shorthorn Raiders and Stalkers
These beastmen are unique in that they avoid rushing into battle to use their Charge ability. Instead, they specialize in targeting foes their allies can't reach in close combat. They are skillful and opportunistic archers and will take cover between their attacks whenever possible.

\columnbreak

<br>

#### Longhorn Tactics
Longhorns make up the bulk of most beastmen warherds. When fighting together, they form a rowdy mob drunk on their confidence and recklessly charging into enemies. If the fight doesn't quickly go in their favor, sobering reality may set in, causing them to break and flee if they don't have a leader keeping them in line.

##### Longhorn Ravagers
These beastmen's signature ability is Swig. They will typically expend a use of the ability just before combat, letting the poisoned condition clear while retaining the temporary hit points. 

In the heat of battle, they will use the Swig ability again if they lose their Primal Fury or they drop below half health. It's important that they use Swig after they've made their attacks for the turn so they can minimize the disadvantage from being poisoned.

Because of their drunken nature, these beastmen will be even more wild and reckless than the rest of their kin, and you can reflect this by having them take more foolhardy actions in combat.

#### Besthorns
Because these elite warriors wear medium armor and don't have the Bestial Ambush trait, they are not as reliant on stealth and ambush tactics as other beastmen. If they're teamed up with other beastmen who have Bestial Ambush, the besthorns will charge the players first. This will allow the sneakier beastmen an opportunity to move around and attack from behind while the players are distracted.

##### Besthorn Manrippers
These beastmen prioritize attacking targets with low Strength so they can best utilize their Hewing Greataxe attacks. However, if the enemies they can reach all have high AC or abilities that make them hard to hit, the manrippers will change their strategy to attacking foes that are grouped up so they can attempt to make use of their Arcing Swing ability.

#### Warhorns and Beastlords
These beastmen leaders fight from within the center of their minions, extending their aura to as many beastmen as possible. Because they're constantly seeking the favor of their dark gods, they will often challenge the most powerful adversaries they can find to prove their worth.

Because of their armor, their ambush options are often limited, and so they typically use the same combat initiation tactics as besthorns.

\pagebreakNum

### Beastmen Loot
Because beastmen are humanoids, most of the valuable goods that can be looted from them are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying, though it is common to harvest horns from their fallen. Most dropped valuables can be found using an **Intelligence (Investigation)** check.

Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.


#### Beastmen Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

<br>

> ##### New Condition: Emboldened  
> This document references the Emboldened condition. 
> * The Emboldened condition always lasts one minute.
> * An Emboldened creature deals additional 7 (2d6) damage when it hits with a attack.
> * At the end of the creature's turn, the Emboldened condition ends early if it missed with all of its attacks that turn, it is charmed or frightened, or is effected by *calm emotions* spell. 
>

## The Dark Omen

The Dark Omen is a figure of dread and awe within the annals of human legend and folklore, a bray speaker whose name is whispered in fearful tones. His physical form is a grotesque testament to his dark powers, marked distinctly by a pair of large, tattered crow wings sprouting from his back. These wings are often kept hidden under his hide cloak, but when outstretched, they are revealed to be black as the deepest night and as ominous as the shadows dancing at the firelight's edge. They are seen as a physical embodiment of his cursed connection to the dark gods.

The coming of The Dark Omen is always foretold by a series of dark portents and ominous signs. In woodland regions, locals speak of strange hoofprints leading up to their door, flocks of crows that blot out the sun, and a sense of dread that settles over the land like a suffocating blanket. These supernatural occurrences have elevated The Dark Omen to a figure of religious superstition and fearful reverence among those living near the forests. Some unfortunate souls may even catch a glimpse of the creature leering from the shadowy forest edge, an event which all but guarantees impending misfortune and doom.

When he emerges from the darkest depths of the ancient forests, The Dark Omen is more than just a leader among the beastmen; he is the harbinger of doom and a prophet of despair. 

### The Dark Omen Art Credit
* Rageblood Shaman - Mike Bierek, Wizards of the Coast


\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

 His origins are shrouded in mystery, with rumors suggesting he was chosen by the dark gods themselves, transformed from a mere beastman into a being of immense mystical power. His eyes are said to blaze with an unholy light, piercing through the shadows of the forest, and his voice carries the weight of prophecy, his words twisting the minds of those who hear them.

The Dark Omen's ruinous reputation is built upon countless desecrated shrines and fallen enemies, his mere presence spreading fear and chaos. He is not only a master of dark sorcery but also a tactician of savage warfare, leading his herds in brutal raids against civilization. His command over the beastmen is absolute, his will enforced not just by strength but by the sheer terror he invokes. In battle, he wields his malevolent magic with devastating effect, cursing his foes and bolstering his followers with the primal fury of the wilds.

Legend has it that The Dark Omen seeks to fulfill a dire prophecy, one that foretells a great reckoning that will engulf the world in chaos and darkness. As he moves unseen through the forest, the beating of his crow wings is said to be an omen of the dark times to come, a reminder that the beastmen are ever waiting at the edge of the civilized lands, ready to reclaim the world in the name of their sinister deities.

* Foul Watcher - Mila Pesic, Wizards of the Coast
* Revenge of Ravens - Dmitry Burmak, Wizards of the Coast

> ___
>
> ***Beast Man.*** The Dark Omen is considered a beast in addition to his humanoid type when determining the effects of features, spells, and abilities such as the *dominate beast* spell.
>
> ***Forest Camouflage.*** The Dark Omen has advantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made to hide in forest terrain.
>
> ***Land's Stride.*** Moving through nonmagical difficult terrain costs The Dark Omen no extra movement.
>
> ***Spellcasting.*** The Dark Omen is a spellcaster. His spellcasting ability is Wisdom (spell save DC 18, +10 to hit with spell attacks). He knows the following spells:
>
> *At will:* *druidcraft*, *find the path*, *mystic signal** (ritual only), *summon flock** (9th level)
>
> ***Unholy Fury (1/day).*** At the start of his turn, The Dark Omen can begin channeling his unholy fury. At the start of each of his turns for the next minute (including the turn he activates this ability), The Dark Omen gains a level of power. He gains the following cumulative benefits for each level of power:
>
> * Access to new spells, each of which he can cast once per use of this feature. These spells don't require material components.
> * He can maintain concentration on an additional spell per level, which can't be broken as a result of taking damage.
> * The Dark Omen and chosen allies he can see within 120 feet with Primal Fury active deal an extra 4 (1d8) necrotic damage on hit with attacks and get +1 to Wisdom checks triggered by Primal Fury abilities, as well as saving throws against being charmed or frightened.
>
> If no creatures fail saving throws against any spell The Dark Omen cast this turn, or if he is charmed, frightened, or has taken 100 or more damage since his last turn, he must make a DC 15 Wisdom check. On a failure, he loses one level of power.
>
> **Unholy Fury Spells Gained Per Level***
> * **1 level of power:** *primal scream*, *withering resolve*
> * **2 levels of power:** *impending doom*, *wind of death*
> * **3 levels of power:** *horrifying laughter*, *pit of shadows*
> * **4 levels of power:** *purple sun*, *savage dominion* 
>
> <br>***Charge.*** If The Dark Omen moves at least 20 ft. straight toward a target and then hits it with a Gore attack on the same turn, the target takes an extra 7 (2d6) piercing damage. If the target is a creature, it must succeed on a DC 16 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +7 to hit, reach 5 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 6 (1d6 + 3) piercing damage.
>
> ***Quarterstaff.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +7 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 6 (1d6 + 3) bludgeoning damage, or 7 (1d8 + 3) bludgeoning damage if wielded with two hands.
>
> ### Legendary Actions
>
> The Dark Omen can take 3 legendary actions, choosing from the options below. Only one legendary action option can be used at a time and only at the end of another creature's turn. The Dark Omen regains spent legendary actions at the start of his turn.
>
> **Swoop.** The Dark Omen moves up to 20 feet without provoking opportunity attacks, then makes a weapon attack.
>
> **Check.** The Dark Omen makes a skill check that would normally require an action.
>
> **Tenacious Will.** If The Dark Omen is suffering from an effect that allows him to make a saving throw as an action or at the beginning or end of his next turn, he may immediately make that save against the effect with advantage. He can use this legendary action while incapacitated.
>
> **Unholy Casting (Costs 3 Actions).** The Dark Omen casts a spell granted by its Unholy Fury ability that he has access to.
>
> **New Spells Found In Spells Section of Document*


\pagebreakNum

### Epic Encounter
If you wish to make The Dark Omen into a threat for end-game players, you can make the following enhancements:

* Increase his hit points to 600
* Increase the AC granted by his natural armor to 17
* Give him proficiency in Strength and Dexterity saving throws (increasing his modifier to +8 for Strength and +7 for Dexterity)
* Increase his CR to 20


### The Dark Omen's Lair
The Dark Omen does not keep a traditional lair or even stay in one area for long. Instead, he roams the land before choosing a location to bring ruination upon. This is usually a relatively isolated village or farmland near woods where he can establish a temporary lair. From here, The Omen slowly begins to sow terror among everyone living nearby.

When fighting within his lair, The Dark Omen's CR increases by 1.

#### Lair Actions

When fighting inside his lair, The Dark Omen can invoke the ambient magic that has saturated his temporary abode to use his lair action. On initiative count 20 (losing initiative ties), The Dark Omen can cause the following effects, even while incapacitated:

Creatures without the Primal Fury or Unholy Fury abilities in the layer must make a DC 15 Wisdom saving throw. On a failure, a creature is overwhelmed by a sense of abject defeat until initiative count 20 on the next round. While overwhelmed this way, a creature can't add their proficiency bonus to saving throws, checks, attack rolls, or their spell save DC for spells they cast. If three or more creatures fail the saving, The Dark Omen gains a level of power for his Unholy Fury trait if the ability is active.

#### Regional Effects
Any region where The Dark Omen dwells for a significant amount of time is warped by his magic, creating one or more of the following effects everywhere within 5 miles of his lair:

* Strange footprints appear across the area, going up vertical surfaces, solid objects, and sometimes mysteriously disappearing with no trace. These footprints prevent The Dark Omen from being tracked except by magical means while in the area.
* Clouds in the sky form into leering horned skulls and other twisted faces.
* Beasts within the area become highly aggressive and agitated, causing creatures other than The Dark Omen to have disadvantage on Wisdom (Animal Handling) checks while in the area.
* Crows and carrion birds become predominant in the area and can telepathically communicate with The Dark Omen while he is in the area.

If Dark Omen dies, these effects fade over the course of 1d10 days.

\columnbreak

##### Dark Omen Adventure Hooks

| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Omen's Shadow:** Rumors spread across the region of unnatural phenomena – crops failing, wildlife behaving erratically, and dark visions plaguing the dreams of the villagers. These signs are believed to herald the arrival of The Dark Omen. The players must investigate these omens, protect the affected communities, and uncover the true intention of The Dark Omen's visitation.|
|  2  |**Pact of the Crow:** A village leader, desperate to protect his people from the beastmen's raids, has struck a dangerous bargain with The Dark Omen. The players are drawn into a complex situation where they must deal with the consequences of the leader's actions and confront The Dark Omen to prevent a greater evil from unfolding. |
|  3  | **The Doomed Village:** A village on the forest’s edge is suffering from a mysterious curse since The Dark Omen was sighted nearby. Villagers are vanishing, and those remaining speak of terrifying nightmares. The players need to break the curse, rescue the missing villagers, and confront the source of this dark magic.   |
|  4  | **The Crow Feather’s Trail:** A series of occult crimes and strange events in a city are linked by a single clue – a crow's feather, a known symbol of The Dark Omen. The players must unravel this mystery, leading them on a trail that connects the city's dark underbelly to the ominous forests and ultimately to The Dark Omen himself.  |

### Dark Omen Tactics
The Dark Omen is a formidable spellcaster who is also adept in melee combat. He specializes in casting spells that are most effective at close range. Thanks to his fly speed, The Dark Omen excels in repositioning himself for optimal attacks and spellcasting.

**Minion Interaction:** While The Dark Omen can be an effective solo encounter, he works best with minions.

#### Spells
The Dark Omen's primary ability is Unholy Frenzy, which enhances his spellcasting power as combat progresses. Creatures attempting to charm, frighten, or interfere with the Dark Omen's ability to make Wisdom checks become his primary targets. The Dark Omen is a tactical spellcaster and avoids using spells on targets likely to resist them.

##### Summon Flock
The Dark Omen can cast this spell at will and should always have it active so that he gains a +12 bonus to Perception, bringing his passive Perception up to 22. Attacks made with this spell also benefit from the Unholy Fury trait.

##### Withering Resolve
Cast this spell on creatures likely to interfere with The Dark Omen's Unholy Frenzy checks, particularly targets lacking proficiency in Wisdom saving throws.

##### Primal Scream
* **Use Case 1:** Cast when it can affect more than two targets.
* **Use Case 2:** Cast if The Dark Omen is airborne and is confronted by another flying opponent with low Constitution.

##### Impending Doom 
Best cast on targets with low Charisma or on those already under the effects of Withering Resolve

##### Wind of Death
Effective when it can hit two or more targets

##### Horrifying Laughter vs. Pit of Shadows
* **Horrifying Laughter:** Preferable when targeting a creature whose saving throw has been lowered, especially if it's already affected by *Withering Resolve* or *Impending Doom*
* **Pit of Shadows:** Generally a better choice when it can affect two or more creatures with lower Dexterity, particularly if no target is affected by *Withering Resolve* or *Impending Doom*

##### Savage Dominion vs. Purple Sun
Both spells are extremely devastating, but their usage depends on specific conditions:

* **Purple Sun:** Cast this spell when Dark Omen has 100 or more hit points and is not suffering from any crippling conditions.


\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

* **Savage Dominion:** Opt for this spell if Dark Omen's action economy is low or he anticipates defeat in the next round. The summoned creature persists even after Dark Omen's demise.

##### Creatures Summoned With Savage Dominion
The preferred creature can depend on the state of the battle:
* **Giant:** Ideal for situations where adversaries excel in avoiding melee combat or are engaged in long-range fighting
* **Jabberwocky:** Ideal for disrupting enemies with its Burble ability and other debilitating effects. Note that the Burble ability can affect anyone in proximity, including The Dark Omen
* **Behemoth:** A versatile choice suited for targeting and consuming individual targets as well as attacking groups with its Rend ability

#### Legendary Actions
When The Dark Omen is not in debilitating terrain and is surrounded by less than two enemies, it primarily uses its legendary actions to cast spells. If The Dark Omen finds itself in debilitating terrain or surrounded by two or more enemies, it will prioritize using its actions to reposition itself. When moving, The Dark Omen aims to move from one target. This strategic movement is designed to maximize the benefits of its Charge ability for its Gore attack at the end of its movement.

### The Dark Omen Loot
Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from The Dark Omen come from what can be harvested from his horns and wings or from relics and blasphemous icons he carries. Most dropped valuables can be found using an **Intelligence (Investigation)** or identified using an **Intelligence (Religion)** check. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### The Dark Omen Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. 


##### The Dark Omen Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 7 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-9  | 1d4(2) 500gp Items |
|  10-12 | 1d4(2) 1,000gp Items | 
|  13-19 | 1d6(3) 1,000gp Items  |  
|  20-24 | 1d6(3) 2,000gp Items |  
|  25+ |  2d4(5) 2,000gp Items |

|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-9  | 1 5,000gp Item |
|  10-13 | 1d4(2) 5,000gp Items | 
|  14-19 | 1d4(2) 10,000gp Items  |

## Jabbersnarls
*Repugnant Monstrosities of Fear & Madness*<br>
**Habitat:** Forest, Swamp, Underdark; **Treasure:** Any <br>
Among the most ancient groves, tainted by the malevolent presence of chaos, countless nightmares have crawled forth from the undergrowth. Yet none are more revolting than the jabbersnarl. Its array of legs—a grotesque mingle of insect and amphibian—rival the thickness of pine trees, each tipped with lethal talons that dig into the ground, ushering the beast forward as it drags its misbegotten, bloated, toad-like frame. Its bulk is so immense that even the mightiest ox would be crushed beneath its girth. Trailing behind, a terrible serpentine tail sways, tipped with a mace-like appendage sporting spiky protrusions as long as a greatsword. Upon its back rest a pair of massive, leathery wings, folded until splayed and bent, inexplicably lifting its disjointed mass into the air.

Most grotesque of all is the creature’s amalgamated head. Large ram horns crown its bulbous skull, beneath which sit sets of slitted eyes, each independently searching for its next meal. When a victim strays into its sight, the jabbersnarl opens its toad-like maw, revealing rows of jagged, shark-like teeth lining the interior. Amidst them, a mass of twitching chelicerae writhes, and between these sits a proboscis-like tongue. This tongue can launch as swiftly as an arrow with deadly precision, ensnaring creatures as strong as a full-grown minotaur and dragging them back to its lethal assortment of teeth. There, they are shredded and swallowed into its cavernous gut—all before most prey even realize their terrible fate.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

Even if a creature manages to strike back at this eclectic array of deadly limbs, the jabbersnarl does not bleed blood. Instead, an acidic slime courses through its veins, spurting from wounds to eat through nearby flesh, wood, and steel. Yet the true lethality of this abominable creature lies in its very presence—for its amalgamated body is a magnification of nature’s most horrifying aspects, and the mere sight of such a horrid miscreation causes madness to run rampant. Those who lay eyes upon the jabbersnarl find their sanity eroded. As their minds break, some drop to the ground, curling into a ball, feebly attempting to process the monstrosity before them. Others gut themselves to escape the odious display, while some sink into such deep denial that they refuse to acknowledge the creature’s existence, even as its corded tongue latches onto them and pulls them to their doom.

jabbersnarls are drawn to the commotions and cries of the beastmen who share their corrupted woods, knowing such sounds lead to bountiful prey upon which they may gorge. This attraction can prove hazardous to the beastmen, for even they, worshippers of chaos’s foul deities, are not immune to the delirium the jabbersnarl’s appearance inspires. If insufficient enemies are present to sate its ravenous hunger, it may turn to feed on the herd that beckoned it. However, powerful Bray-Speakers can direct its unearthly cravings, steering it toward foes while ensuring it keeps a wide berth from the rest of the war party. When such manipulations succeed, the warherd greets the occasion with joyful braying, watching the misshapen figure of the jabbersnarl tumble from the sky, crashing into the midst of a disciplined army. All order shatters, replaced by hysteria as the beast wreaks its havoc.


<img src='https://cdn.cardsrealm.com/images/cartas/ons-onslaught/en/crop-med/towering-baloth-292.jpeg?8764' style='position:absolute; top:-55px; right:-0px; width:820px; transform: scaleX(-1)' />

> - **Damage Resistances** Psychic  
> - **Senses** Blindsight 30 ft., Darkvision 120 ft., Passive Perception 13  
> - **Challenge** 15 (13,000 XP)  &emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +5  
> ___  
>  
> ***Visage of Madness.*** The jabbersnarl emits an aura in a 60-foot emanation from itself. *Wisdom Saving Throw:* DC 18, each enemy that starts its turn in the emanation and can see the jabbersnarl. *Failure:* The creature can't take reactions until the start of its next turn and rolls a d6 to determine its actions during that turn. *Fails By 5 or More:* The creature rolls 2d6 instead. *Fails By 10 or More:* The creature rolls 3d6 instead. <br> Unless surprised, a creature can avert its eyes to avoid the saving throw at the start of its turn. If the creature does so, it can't see the jabbersnarl until the start of its next turn, when it can avert its eyes again. If the creature looks at the jabbersnarl in the meantime, it must immediately make the save. 
>  
> ***Hissing Blood.*** When the jabbersnarl takes slashing, piercing, or bludgeoning damage, each other creature in a 10-foot emanation from the jabbersnarl is covered in acid until it or another creature uses its action to scrape or wash the acid off. At the end of a creature’s turn, if it is covered in acid this way, it takes 10 (3d6) acid damage.  
>  
> ***Land's Stride.*** Moving through nonmagical difficult terrain costs the jabbersnarl no extra movement.  
>
> ***Limited Flight.*** The jabbersnarl falls if it ends its turn in the air while nothing else is holding it aloft. It takes no fall damage from falling this way.
>
> ### Actions  
>  
> ***Multiattack.*** The jabbersnarl makes three attacks: one with its Tongue, one with its Claws, and one with its Tail.  
>  
> ***Tongue.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +10 to hit, reach 30 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 10 (3d6) poison damage. The target must make a *Strength Saving Throw:* DC 18. *Failure:* It is pulled to a space within 5 feet of the jabbersnarl.  
>  
> ***Claws.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +10 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 21 (3d10 + 5) piercing damage plus 10 (3d6) poison damage, and the target is grappled (escape DC 18) by one of the jabbersnarl’s three limbs.  
>  
> ***Tail.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +10 to hit, reach 20 ft., one target. *Hit:* 32 (5d10 + 5) bludgeoning damage. If the target is a creature, it must make a *Strength Saving Throw:* DC 18. *Failure:* It is knocked prone. *Fails by 5 or more:* It can't stand up until the end of its next turn.  
>  
> ### Bonus Actions  
>  
> ***Swallow.*** *Dexterity Saving Throw:* DC 18, one Large or smaller creature grappled by the jabbersnarl (it can have up to four creatures swallowed at a time). *Failure:* The creature is swallowed, and the grapple ends. The swallowed creature is blinded and restrained, has total cover against attacks and other effects outside the jabbersnarl, and takes 17 (5d6) acid damage at the start of each of the jabbersnarl's turns. <Br> If the jabbersnarl takes 30 or more damage in a single turn from a creature inside, it makes a *Constitution Saving Throw:* DC 15. *Failure:* The jabbersnarl regurgitates all swallowed creatures, which fall prone in a space within 10 feet of the jabbersnarl. If the jabbersnarl dies, a swallowed creature is no longer restrained and can escape from the corpse by using 10 feet of movement, exiting prone.  

</span>

> ##### Lingering Madness
> If you wish for the jabbersnarls to have more potent effects beyond combat, you can have creatures that fail their Visage of Madness saving throw by 10 or more suffer from Indefinite Madness until dispel evil and good is cast on them.

\columnbreak

> ##### Minions of Madness
> In the standard stat block for the jabbersnarls, only enemies are affected by its Visage of Madness. However, if you wish to emphasize the jabbersnarl as a true creature of madness, you can have its allies affected as well. Depraved allies (such as Beastmen) can be somewhat tolerant of the jabbersnarl's presence—forcing them to still make the saving throw, but granting them advantage on the roll.
Allies that have already completely lost their minds (such as Spawns of Chaos) remain unaffected.




\pagebreakNum

### Madness Effects Table  

| Number Rolled | Name        | Effect |
|:---:|:-----------|:-----------|
|  1  | Stable     | The creature acts as normal. |
|  2  | Agitated    | The creature must take the Attack action or cast a spell that deals damage. |
|  3  | Fixated    | The creature must spend 2 feet of movement for every 1 foot it moves when moving away from any creatures hostile to it that it is aware of. |
|  4  | Trepidation | The creature must spend 2 feet of movement for every 1 foot it moves when moving closer to any creatures hostile to it that it is aware of. |
|  5  | Paranoid   | The creature considers no other creature an ally, refusing help and being unable to benefit from the spells and effects of allies. |
|  6  | Lonely    | The creature has disadvantage on attack rolls and checks unless it is within 5 feet of an ally that isn't incapacitated. |
|  7  | Dizzy      | The creature uses half it's movement to travel in a random direction, determined by rolling a d8. It can then take the rest of its turn as normal. |
|  8  | Babble     | The creature yells at the top of its lungs. It can't cast spells with verbal components, speak, eat, or drink until the start of its next turn. |
| 9  | Blurred Vision     | The creatrue unable to see anything farther than 10 feet away until the start of it's next turn. |
<br>

> ##### New Condition:  Dazed 
> A dazed creature can’t take reactions and on its turn, it must choose whether it gets a move, an action, or a bonus action; it gets only one of the three.

\columnbreak

<br><br>

| Number Rolled | Name        | Effect |
|:---:|:-----------|:-----------|
|  10  | Dull-Witted | The creature can make only one attack during the turn and can only cast cantrips. |
| 11  | Huddle     | The creature falls prone and can't stand up for the rest of its turn. |
| 12  | Addled     | Until the end of the turn, the creature is dazed (condition described below) and can't concentrate. |
| 13  | Frantic    | The creature must take the Dash, Dodge, or Disengage action this turn. |
| 14  | Shivers    | The creature drops whatever it is holding. It can't pick up items, wield weapons, or cast spells with somatic components. |
| 15  | Denial     | The creature can't see or hear any creatures hostile to it until the start of its next turn. |
| 16  | Violent   | The creature moves toward the nearest creature it is aware of and then uses its action to make a single attack if the target is within range. |
| 17  | Penance    | The creature uses it's action to make an attack with whatever it is holding against itself, automatically hitting. |
| 18 +  | Catatonia | The creature is stunned until the start of its next turn. |

\pagebreakNum


### Broodmothers & Their Spawn
Due to their twisted appearance and the maddening effect they have on the mind when observed, little is known about the jabbersnarls beyond their capacity to kill and the insanity that springs from their grotesque nature. The question of how these creatures came to be—or how they reproduce—has never been truly answered. jabbersnarls have never been found living in pairs, nor has any kind of egg or newborn ever been discovered.

Some speak of creatures referred to as "toadlets"—smaller, stunted versions of the jabbersnarl whose underdeveloped wings cannot lift them into the air—claiming these to be juvenile specimens of the species. However, the most chilling accounts come from the scattered testimonies of hunters who, after venturing into remote wilderness, returned days later in a state of incurable delirium.
Committed to asylums, these lunatics share one disturbing commonality in their wild ravings: a massive creature that spews forth writhing hordes of larvae from its porous skin—parasitic spawn that latch onto victims, feeding on their sanity. Yet, as with all things told by unhinged minds, such ghastly statements remain far from reliable, dismissed as mere delusions by most learned scholars.

\columnbreak

> *In a lonesome hill-side, shrouded in woodland untrodden by the steps of men for untold ages, there lieth a cavern. Fain doth it hide its maw, glimpsed only through the thick-leaved bower by eyes full keen beneath the moon’s argent sheen, for by some fell decree, its yawnéd gate doth wither in the sun’s golden gleam. Shouldst thou dare to tread within that shadowed cleft, the air waxeth hot and reeketh with damp, swirling as though it were the very breath of a ravenous fiend. Were this not enough to send back any wight of sound wit, then let the walls, hewn as from wax riven by jaggéd talons, serve as harbinger of doom.*
> 
> *Yet, if these dread signs stir not thy heart to quail, and still thy feet do press onward into the bosom of the earth, a chamber shalt thou find, and therein folly’s lone guerdon. There doth crouch a misshapen bulk, its wretched limbs folded ‘neath its bulk. Eyes slit and yellow awake at thy trespass, and limbs spread wide whilst its vile flesh doth quiver and pulse like the fretful sea. From its hide burst forth foul maggots, armed with needle-rimméd maw, spilling as sweat from a plague-ridden wretch. These loathsome spawn creep nigh, gibbering as the kin of newborn horrors doth fall upon thee. If thought canst thou muster in the midst of such madness, it should be to loosen thy bow and let fly thy shafts into the maker of this accurséd brood, to dim those eyes slit and yellow that fix upon thee. Yet arrows that strike deep pierce but to wretched ends, for such wounds gape wide and vomit forth yet more of her slinking progeny.*
> 
> *Then doth the loathly thing, with eyes slit and yellow, unfurl wings vast as a ship’s sail, spanning its lair, and shake its ungodly frame, flinging its young in all wise as a tempest of noisome rain. Its foul issue o’ertaketh thee, a gaping maw fastening to thy head, feasting upon such scraps of reason as yet linger, unclaimed by those eyes, slit and yellow, that have taken so much. What then betid, I cannot tell, for I wakened upon the floor of mine own cot, leagues yonder, my flesh fouled with the filth of far wayfaring and riven with woe. How I came hither, I know not, and though time may mend my frame, the scars of my soul shall not so lightly fade. No soft bed, nor gentle touch, nor potent draught shall grant me ease. I crave only that Death may wrest from me the memory of that Broodmother, her swarming get, and those eyes, slit and yellow, that still do burn in my mind from that cavern in the lonesome hill-side, veiled by woodland untrodden by men, and that shouldst yet remain untrodden for ages uncounted.*
> 
> **-Last writing of the Huntsman Leopold Totleben before hanging himself.**

> ***Aura of Madness.*** The jabbersnarl emits an aura in a 60-foot emanation from itself. *Wisdom Saving Throw:* DC 19, each enemy that starts its turn in the emanation. *Failure:* The creature can't take reactions until the start of its next turn and rolls a d6 to determine its actions during that turn. *Fails By 5 or More:* The creature rolls 2d6 instead. *Fails By 10 or More:* The creature rolls 3d6 instead. Unless surprised, a creature can avert its eyes to avoid the saving throw at the start of its turn. If the creature does so, it can't see the jabbersnarl until the start of its next turn, when it can avert its eyes again. If the creature looks at the jabbersnarl in the meantime, it must immediately make the save.  
>  
> ***Infested Blood.*** When the jabbersnarl takes slashing, piercing, or bludgeoning damage, it creates a **Maddening Larva** (stat block on next page) in an unoccupied space within 15 feet of her. The maddening larva remain for one hour or until the jabbersnarl dies. They act on initiative count 0 (losing initiative ties). The jabbersnarl can have up to thirty maddening larva at a time with any of its abilities.  
>  
> ***Land's Stride.*** Moving through nonmagical difficult terrain costs the jabbersnarl no extra movement.
>
> ***Limited Flight.*** The jabbersnarl falls if it ends its turn in the air while nothing else is holding it aloft. It takes no fall damage from falling this way.
>
> ### Actions  
>  
> ***Multiattack.*** The jabbersnarl makes three attacks: one with its Tongue, one with its Claws, and one with its Tail.  
>  
> ***Tongue.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +11 to hit, reach 30 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 10 (3d6) poison damage. The target must make a *Strength Saving Throw:* DC 19. *Failure:* It is pulled to a space within 5 feet of the jabbersnarl.  
>  
> ***Claws.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +11 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 21 (3d10 + 5) piercing damage plus 10 (3d6) poison damage, and the target is grappled (escape DC 19) by one of the jabbersnarl’s three limbs.  
>  
> ***Tail.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +11 to hit, reach 20 ft., one target. *Hit:* 32 (5d10 + 5) bludgeoning damage. The target must make a *Strength Saving Throw:* DC 19. *Failure:* It is knocked prone. *Fails By 5 or More:* It can't stand up until the end of its next turn.  
>  
> ### Bonus Actions  
>  
> ***Swallow.*** *Dexterity Saving Throw:* DC 19, one Large or smaller creature grappled by the jabbersnarl (it can have up to four creatures swallowed at a time). *Failure:* The creature is swallowed, and the grapple ends. The swallowed creature is blinded and restrained, has total cover against attacks and other effects outside the jabbersnarl, and takes 17 (5d6) acid damage at the start of each of the jabbersnarl's turns. <Br> If the jabbersnarl takes 30 or more damage in a single turn from a creature inside, it makes a *Constitution Saving Throw:* DC 15. *Failure:* The jabbersnarl regurgitates all swallowed creatures, which fall prone in a space within 10 feet of it. If the jabbersnarl dies, a swallowed creature is no longer restrained and can escape from the corpse by using 10 feet of movement, exiting prone.  
>  
> ### Repugnant Spawning  
> On initiative count 20 (losing initiative ties), the jabbersnarl spews out 3 + 1d4 **Maddening Larva** (stat block at the end of the document) in unoccupied spaces within 15 feet of it. If the jabbersnarl is bloodied, it creates 6 + 1d4 instead. The maddening larva remain for one hour or until the jabbersnarl dies. They act on initiative count 0 (losing initiative ties). The jabbersnarl can have up to thirty maddening larva at a time with any of its abilities.

On its turn, the larva can detach itself from the target by using 5 feet of movement. When it dies, the larva detaches from any creature it is attached to.

Then, if the jabbersnarl broodmother is suffering from an effect that allows it to make a saving throw or check as an action or at the beginning or end of her next turn, it may immediately make that save.

### Jabbersnarl Tactics

All jabbersnarls tend to place themselves in the center of the largest horde of enemies, using their tongue to pull distant targets toward them. They prioritize attacking creatures with low Dexterity scores or those refusing to look at them.
If overwhelmed—or once they’ve gorged themselves—they may reposition, but they will never flee unless they already have a meal in tow.

#### Broodmother Tactics
The Broodmother’s larvae obey her every command instinctively. She will spread out her spaw to make sure that they are not hit by a single AOE spell and killed. Having them each go for different targets.

##### Jabbersnarl Adventure Hooks

| 1d6  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Screaming Fog:** A choking fog has settled on a trade route through the woods. Merchants speak of hallucinations, missing companions, and haunting screams in the mist. In truth, a jabbersnarl has made the fogbound glade its hunting ground, and its very presence twists the minds of those who enter. The players must either guide a caravan safely through or take on a bounty to clear the cursed pass.  |
|  2  | **The Beast That Ate the Cult:** A newly risen cult worshiping a chaos deity has vanished from their woodland altar. Their camp is now a gore-splattered crater. Strange claw marks and slime trails suggest they summoned something they couldn’t control. The players must piece together the ritual, learn what was brought into the world, and determine whether it can be banished—or if it’s already too late.  |
|  3  | **The Beastmen’s Bargain:** Beastmen warbands have been striking settlements with unprecedented coordination. Reports mention not just the usual braying hordes—but also something worse crashing down into the battlefield. A Bray-Speaker has learned to call down a jabbersnarl and direct it toward enemy forces. The players must break the pact or slay the speaker to stop the next town from falling into madness and ruin. |
|  4  | **The Stolen Toadling:** A group of reckless cultists has stolen an unhatched jabbersnarl spawn from a beastmen warherd. The players are hired to retrieve it—either by the cult's enemies or by the desperate cultists themselves, who didn’t realize what they were dealing with. The egg is hatching fast, and the players may soon face a ravenous, jabbersnarl toadling that’s already oozing madness. |
|  5  |  **Ravings of the Returned:** A renowned ranger stumbles back into town, bloodied and broken after a solo expedition into the wilds. His mind is shattered, and he speaks only in gibberish—until he begins screaming about a mountainous toad-beast that "bled madness" and birthed horrors from its own flesh. The players are hired to retrace his steps and uncover the truth, leading them deep into uncharted woods... where the Broodmother waits, surrounded by swarms of writhing Toadlets and parasite-larvae.  |
|  6  | **The Carnival Cradle.** A traveling freak show boasts a new “star attraction”: a caged horror they claim to be a genuine chaos beast. In truth, it’s a juvenile Toadlet spawned by a Broodmother hiding in the dark woods nearby, drawn to the sounds and smells of the traveling carnival. As the players investigate the unnatural changes among the performers and guests, the Broodmother arrives to reclaim her spawn—with an army of wriggling horrors in tow. |

\columnbreak

### Jabbersnarl Loot
Valuable jabbersnarl loot typically comes from harvested materials and usually requires a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Arcana)** check. You may also allow players proficient in specific tools to harvest relevant items (e.g., a **Wisdom (Leatherworker’s Tools)** check to gather Hide). 

Alternatively, you can roll for loot randomly using a flat modifier.

##### Jabbersnarl Loot (Avg. 1,850gp)

| Looting Check Result <br> or 1d20 + 5 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-8  | 1 500gp Item (500gp) + <br> 2d6(7) 50gp Items (350gp) |
|  9-12 | 1d4(2) 500gp Items (1,000gp) + <br> 2d6(10) 50gp Items (500gp)  | 
|  13-19 | 1 1,000gp Item (1,000gp) + <br> 3d8(13) 50gp Items (650gp) |  
|  20-23 | 1d4(2) 2,000gp Items (4,000gp) + <br> 2d6(7) 100gp Items (700gp) |  
|  24+ |  1 2,000gp Item (2,000gp) + <br> 2d6(7) 200gp Items (1,400gp) |

#### Optional: Describing Looted Materials
If you’re not interested in the specifics, simply say the party collected materials worth the rolled gp value. If you want more detail, the tables below suggest materials for different gp values by creature. They also provide **Example Names** and **Quality Descriptors** for items worth **half** or **twice** the table's gp value.

For example, a 100gp Bone item from a jabbersnarl could be a Jabbersnarl Fang, a 50gp version might be a Cracked Jabbersnarl Fang, and a 200gp version could be a Superior Jabbersnarl Fang.

***When To Use Descriptions.*** You can describe these items during looting, when selling them, or when crafting, but it's best not to make players track long descriptive names. Only use as much detail as is needed when needed.

#### Optional: Magic Loot for Item Crafting
If you plan to use these creatures’ loot for crafting magic items, consult the Magic Themes table for thematic suggestions. The **Magic Theme** column helps align the crafted item’s effects with the creature’s nature, while the **Example Descriptor** suggests how to describe the loot's magical quality. Magic loot can span one or multiple themes.
 
For example, Chaotic loot could be used to craft items that warp space or time or produce unpredictable effects.
 
***Random Magic Ingredients.***
To introduce randomness to how often magic loot is found, roll a percentile die along with the normal loot roll to see if magic loot is found. There's a suggested probability at the top of the table.

##### Jabbersnarl Magic Themes 
**Suggested Chance of Finding Magic Loot: 75%**
|1d4 | Magic Theme | Example Descriptor | 
|:--:|:---:|:-----------:|
| 1-4 <br>  | Chaotic (Eldritch/Realty-Warping)| Warped| 
| 4   | Primal (Druidic/Nature)  | Primeval|  

***Magic Loot GP Values.*** The value of magic ingredients depends on your crafting system. Subtract their cost from the normal loot’s gp value. If the ingredient is worth significantly more, subtract it from the next treasure hoard instead.

## Megataurs

Megataurs are colossal four-armed <br> monstrosities that tower over their <br> beastmen kin, feared and revered in equal <br> measure. These giant creatures are believed <br> to be former minotaurs who underwent extreme <br> mutations due to the overconsumption of tainted <br> flesh or other eldritch substances. This consumption <br> led to grotesque transformations, amplifying their already formidable strength and size, and giving them their terrifying new form.

Two of the megataur's arms end in massive, bone-like blades, perfect for cleaving through armor and flesh alike. The other two arms are used to grab and shovel as much flesh into their fanged maw as possible, feeding their insatiable hunger. Their monstrous form and ravenous appetite make them nearly uncontrollable, a fact that only the most powerful beastmen chieftains and shamans can overcome. Those who can control a megataur wield it as a living weapon of war, unleashing its fury upon their enemies.

In combat, megataurs are devastating forces of nature. They rush into masses of enemies with terrifying speed, bulldozing through ranks and causing chaos and panic. Their bladed arms swing with destructive force, while their other arms grab and swallow foes whole. The sight of a Megataur rampaging across the battlefield is enough to break the spirit of even the most stalwart defenders, leaving a trail of destruction and carnage in its wake. These beasts are not just instruments of war; they are the embodiment of the beastmen's endless hunger, unleashed upon the world in a frenzy of blood and violence.

***The Blood Brute.*** The Blood Brute is a particularly fearsome megataur, having received dark blessings from a demonic lord of war and bloodlust. These unholy gifts have intensified the creature's already insatiable hunger for flesh and unquenchable thirst for blood. No matter how many foes it consumes, The Blood Brute's ravenous appetite can never be sated, driving it into a perpetual frenzy. This cursed existence makes The Blood Brute an even more terrifying force on the battlefield. Its eyes burn with an unholy fire, and its roars echo with the rage of its demonic patron. The Blood Brute's presence is a harbinger of unparalleled carnage, as it rampages through enemy ranks, driven by an endless desire to feed and kill. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

> ##### New Condition: Berserk
> Berserk creatures gain the following effects unless an ability states otherwise:
>  * The creature can only use its movement to move closer to an enemy it can see or hear.
>  * The creature can only use its action, bonus action, and reaction to make melee attacks or move closer to an enemy it can see or hear.
>  * The creature can't maintain concentration on spells or other effects.
>  * The creature can't be frightened or charmed.

### Megatuar Tactics
#### Combat Initiation
* Use Rushing Gore to close distance when enemies are out of reach.
* Once in melee range, target the physically strongest creature for blade arm attacks.
* Simultaneously attempt to grasp and swallow nearby, physically weaker creatures.

#### Rejuvenation Strategy
* The megataur requires creatures in its stomach to activate rejuvenation.
* If its health falls to half or less and there are no enemy creatures in its stomach or nearby, start swallowing weaker allied creatures to heal.

##### Megataur Adventure Hooks

| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Ritual of Gorging :** The players discover that a cult of beastmen shamans is performing a dark ritual to transform captured minotaurs into megataurs so they may provide them to beastman warlords they deem worthy. |
|  2  | **The Megataur Labyrinth:** Deep beneath an ancient forest lies a maze-like network of tunnels that have become the lair of a megataur who preys on travelers and is said to guard foul relics of the dark gods.  |
|  3  | **The Flesh Pit:** The players learn of a secretive beastmen arena where captured enemies are fed to a megataur in gruesome ritual combat. |
|  4  | **The Blood Pact:** A powerful beastman warlord has struck a dark pact with a demonic lord, resulting in the creation of a megataur known as The Blood Brute who, he plans to use as the lynchpin in his upcoming invasion.  |

> ## Megataur
> *Huge monstrosity (beastman), chaotic evil*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 15 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 273 (26d10+130)
> - **Speed** 50 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|24 (+7)|10 (+0)|20 (+5)|6 (-2)|10 (+0)|8 (-1)|
>___
> - **Saving Throws** Int +3, Cha +4, Wis +5
> - **Skills** Athletics +12, Perception +10, Intimidation +10, Stealth +5, Survival +10
> - **Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 20
> - **Languages** Abyssal
> - **Challenge** 16 (15,000 XP) &emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +5
> ___
>
> ***Blood Greed.*** At the end of each turn, if the megataur dealt damage to a creature this turn, it goes berserk until the end of its next turn. While berserk, it deals an extra 9 (2d8) damage on hit with weapon attacks.
>
> ***Keen Smell.*** The megataur has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on smell.
>
> ***Labyrinthine Recall.*** The megataur can perfectly recall any path it has traveled.
>
> ***Land's Stride.*** Moving through nonmagical difficult terrain does not cost the megataur extra movement.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The megataur makes two attacks with its Blade Arms. It can then use its Swallow or make two fist attacks.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +12 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 21 (3d10 + 7) piercing damage.
>
> ***Blade Arm.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +12 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 25 (3d12 + 7) slashing damage.
>
> ***Fist.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +12 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 12 (2d4 + 7) bludgeoning damage. If the target is Large or smaller, it is grappled (escape DC 20). The megataur has two fists, each of which can grapple only one target.
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +12 to hit, reach 5 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 32 (4d12 + 6) piercing damage. If the megataur moved at least 20 feet straight toward the target immediately before the hit, the target takes an extra 26 (4d12) piercing damage. If the target is a creature, it must succeed on a DC 20 Strength saving throw or be pushed up to 10 feet away and knocked prone.
>
> ***Swallow.*** The megataur makes one bite attack against each Large or smaller target it is grappling. If the attack hits, the target is swallowed, and the grapple ends. The swallowed creature is blinded and restrained and has total cover against attacks and other effects outside the megataur. At the start of each of the megataur's turns, each swallowed creature then takes 21 (4d6) acid damage. The megataur regains 5 hit points for each creature damaged this way. If the creature is reduced to 0 hit points by the acid damage, it dies, and its body is dissolved. The megataur dies only if it starts its turn with 0 hit points and doesn't regain hit points from this feature.
>
> If the megataur takes 30 damage or more on a single turn from a creature inside it, the megataur must succeed on a DC 15 Constitution saving throw at the end of that turn or regurgitate all swallowed creatures, which fall prone in a space within 10 feet of the megataur. If the megataur dies, a swallowed creature is no longer restrained by it and can escape from the corpse by using 10 feet of movement, exiting prone.
>
> ### Bonus Action
>
> ***Rushing Gore.*** When the megataur takes the Dash action, it can make a Gore attack.

> ## Megataur, Blood Brute
> *Huge monstrosity (beastman), chaotic evil*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 15 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 399 (38d10+190)
> - **Speed** 50 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|24 (+7)|10 (+0)|20 (+5)|6 (-2)|10 (+0)|8 (-1)|
>___
> - **Saving Throws** Dex +7, Int +5, Cha +6, Wis +7
> - **Skills** Athletics +14, Perception +14, Intimidation +13, Stealth +7, Survival +14
> - **Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 24
> - **Languages** Abyssal
> - **Challenge** 21 (33,000 XP) &emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +7
> ___
>
> ***Blood Greed.*** At the end of each turn, if the megataur dealt damage to a creature this turn, it goes berserk until the end of its next turn. While berserk, it deals an extra 9 (2d8) damage on hit with weapon attacks.
>
> ***Keen Smell.*** The megataur has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on smell.
>
> ***Labyrinthine Recall.*** The megataur can perfectly recall any path it has traveled.
>
> ***Land's Stride.*** Moving through nonmagical difficult terrain does not cost the megataur extra movement.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The megataur makes two attacks with its Blade Arms.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +14 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 22 (3d10 + 7) piercing damage.
>
> ***Blade Arm.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +14 to hit, reach 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 26 (3d12 + 7) slashing damage.
>
> ***Fist.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +14 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 12 (2d4 + 7) bludgeoning damage. If the target is Large or smaller, it is grappled (escape DC 23). The megataur has two Fists, each of which can grapple only one target.
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +14 to hit, reach 5 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 33 (4d12 + 7) piercing damage. If the megataur moved at least 20 feet straight toward the target immediately before the hit, the target takes an extra 26 (4d12) piercing damage. If the target is a creature, it must succeed on a DC 22 Strength saving throw or be pushed up to 10 feet away and knocked prone.
>
> ***Swallow.*** The megataur makes one bite attack against each Large or smaller target it is grappling. If the attack hits, the target is swallowed, and the grapple ends. The swallowed creature is blinded and restrained and has total cover against attacks and other effects outside the megataur. At the start of each of the megataur's turns, each swallowed creature gains a level of heat and then takes 14 (4d6) fire damage for each level of heat it has. The megataur regains 5 hit points for each creature damaged this way. A creature loses all stacks of heat once it is no longer restrained by the megataur. If the creature is reduced to 0 hit points by the fire damage, it dies, and its body is dissolved. The megataur dies only if it starts its turn with 0 hit points and doesn't regain hit points from this feature.
>
> If the megataur takes 30 damage or more on a single turn from a creature inside it, the megataur must succeed on a DC 15 Constitution saving throw at the end of that turn or regurgitate all swallowed creatures, which fall prone in a space within 10 feet of the megataur. If the megataur dies, a swallowed creature is no longer restrained by it and can escape from the corpse by using 10 feet of movement, exiting prone.
>
> ### Bonus Action
>
> ***Rushing Gore.*** When the megataur takes the Dash action, it can make a Gore attack.
>
> ### Legendary Actions
> The megataur can take 3 legendary actions, choosing from the options below. Only one legendary action option can be used at a time and only at the end of another creature's turn. The megataur regains spent legendary actions at the start of its turn.
>
> **Blood Call.** The megataur chooses a creature that just took its turn, which it can see within 120 feet of it, calling it into battle by having the creature's own blood turn on it. At the start of the creature's next turn, the target may move on its turn toward the megataur by the most direct route, trying to get within 10 feet of it. The creature can then take the rest of its turn as normal, except it can't move away from the megataur willingly and can't teleport. If it doesn't choose to move this way, it takes 27 (5d10) force damage instead.
>
> **Check.** The megataur makes a skill check that would normally require an action.
>
> **Lunging Grasp.** The megataur moves up to 25 feet and then may make a Fist attack against a creature that just took its turn.
>
> **Swallow.** The megataur uses the Swallow action.
>
> **Tenacious Will.** If the megataur is suffering from an effect that allows it to make a saving throw as an action or at the beginning or end of its next turn, it may immediately make that save against the effect with advantage. It can use this legendary action while incapacitated.

### Megataur Loot
The valuable items looted from rat ogres will generally come from whatever can be harvested from them. This harvesting can usually be done using a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Nature)** check. However, you may allow players proficient with specific tools to harvest items related to that tool. For example, a character might make a Wisdom (Leathworker’s Tools) check to harvest hide. 
Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

## Minotaurs

Minotaurs are towering monstrosities among the beastmen, standing twice as tall as a man with bodies rippling with massive muscles and heads resembling those of fierce, fanged bulls. Their bull heads are equipped with sharp teeth, perfect for tearing at flesh and making them even more fearsome in close combat. Their sheer size and strength make them formidable foes on any battlefield, their presence alone often causing enemies to falter in fear. Though they possess immense physical power, minotaurs are known to be even less intelligent than their beastmen kin, relying on brute force and primal instincts rather than cunning or strategy.

In battle, minotaurs are driven by an insatiable hunger for flesh, with a particular preference for human flesh. This ravenous appetite fuels their ferocity, and once they taste blood, they are thrown into a wild frenzy. Their charges are devastating, capable of breaking through enemy lines and causing chaos and destruction. The sight of a blood-crazed minotaur rampaging through a battlefield is enough to turn the tide of combat in favor of the beastmen.

\columnbreak

___
> ## Minotaur
> *Large monstrosity (beastman), chaotic evil*

>
> ***Labyrinthine Recall.*** The minotaur can perfectly recall any path it has traveled.
>
> ***Land's Stride.*** Moving through nonmagical difficult terrain does not cost the minotaur extra movement.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 13 (2d8 + 4) piercing damage. If the minotaur moved at least 20 feet straight toward the target immediately before the hit, the target takes an extra 9 (2d8) piercing damage. If the target is a creature, it must succeed on a DC 14 Strength saving throw or be pushed up to 10 feet away and knocked prone.
>
> ***Greataxe.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 17 (2d12 + 4) slashing damage.
>

<br>

> ##### New Condition: Berserk
> Berserk creatures gain the following effects unless an ability states otherwise:
> * The creature can only use its movement to move closer to an enemy it can see or hear.
> * The creature can only use its action, bonus action, and reaction to make melee attacks or move closer to an enemy it can see or hear.
> * The creature can't maintain concentration on spells or other effects.
> * The creature can't be frightened or charmed.

\pagebreakNum

Minotaurs hold a special place in the dark pantheon of beastmen worship. They are often called upon by their dark gods to serve as guardians of sacred, unholy sites hidden deep underground or within the darkest parts of the woods. These sites are often maze-like, labyrinthine structures created through the twisted influence of the dark gods. Minotaurs navigate these unholy labyrinths with unnatural ease, hunting down intruders with relentless determination. 

Despite the fear they inspire, powerful beastmen leaders will summon minotaurs to join them in battle, luring them with promises of fresh meat and the chance to sate their bloodlust. Other beastmen tread carefully around these hulking brutes, aware of their unpredictable nature and the devastation they can unleash.


Minotaurs who frequently participate in the wars of the beastmen and have gorged on the flesh of countless enemies become more powerful and are referred to as Flesh Gorgers. These monstrous brutes grow even larger and more muscled, their already formidable strength becoming even more devastating. Their fanged bull heads become more menacing, with teeth stained from the blood of their countless victims. The insatiable hunger that drives them intensifies, turning them into relentless engines of destruction on the battlefield. Flesh Gorgers are feared by both enemies and their fellow beastmen, their bloodlust and ferocity making them nearly unstoppable forces of nature. Their presence in a battle often signals an impending massacre, as they tear through foes with terrifying ease, leaving carnage in their wake.

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

The Butchers are a notorious group of minotaurs, renowned for their unparalleled brutality and efficiency in combat. Each member of this dreaded band wields a massive meat cleaver, a weapon perfectly suited to their immense strength and savage nature. These cleavers are capable of hewing through flesh, bone, and armor with horrifying ease. When the Butchers charge into battle, their cleavers flash through the air, leaving a trail of blood and dismembered bodies in their wake. Their brutal fighting style and sheer ferocity ensure that few can stand against them for long.

Unlike other minotaurs driven by the immediate need to sate their hunger, the Butchers are known for slaughtering far more foes than they can devour at one time. Entire villages fall to their rampages, leaving behind a grisly tableau of carnage. The Butchers string up the remaining corpses, leaving them to rot as a grim warning to others and as a gruesome larder they can return to whenever they please. These horrific displays serve both as a deterrent to would-be challengers and as a testament to their savage dominance. The Butchers' reign of terror spreads fear far and wide, with their name becoming synonymous with relentless slaughter and unending horror. The sight of their macabre handiwork marks the territory of the Butchers, reminding all who see it of the monstrous appetites and barbaric cruelty that define these fearsome minotaurs.

#### Minotaur Commanders


Minotaur commanders, known as Warbulls, are seasoned veterans blessed by the dark gods, their strength and resilience elevated to supernatural levels. These commanders become engines of brutal destruction, their colossal forms and overwhelming power making them effective leaders despite their limited intelligence. The greatest among them, the Doombulls, are towering figures of unrelenting wrath and devastating might. Revered and feared, Doombulls inspire a frenzied bloodlust in their followers, driving them to fight with reckless abandon and brutal efficiency. Their formidable presence alone can turn the tide of battle, as their followers are Emboldened by the sheer power and ferocity they witness.

Both Warbulls and Doombulls lead through raw power and presence, often commanding from the front lines where their followers can see their unmatched might firsthand. Their roars and bellows incite their beastmen hordes to unparalleled ferocity, turning warbands into unstoppable tides of destruction. While lacking in subtlety and strategic cunning, their straightforward approach of overwhelming force is brutally effective. The sight of a Doombull leading a charge signals the arrival of chaos and carnage on an unprecedented scale, striking fear into the hearts of even the most seasoned warriors. These commanders rely not on complex strategies but on their ability to inspire terror and bloodlust, ensuring that their armies fight with the same relentless savagery that defines them.

### Minotaur Tactics
#### Common Traits
* Formidable melee fighters.
* Lower health but higher damage output.
* Possess Blood Greed trait, increasing damage and appetite for flesh.
* After a kill, they may gorge on the prey rather than pursue other nearby enemies.

#### Minotaur Combat Style
* Favors a full gore attack, knocking targets back 10 feet.
* Typically backs up to charge again, unless blood greed is active.
* When blood greed is active, uses a greataxe or charges at an accessible enemy, risking opportunity attacks.

#### Minotaur Butcher
* Higher defense than regular Minotaurs.
* Blood Greed activation enhances Hewing Cleaver attack and triggers Blood Regeneration for better survivability.

#### Gorebull
* Capable of making two attacks per turn; first a gore to knock a target prone, then a greataxe attack with advantage.
* Can charge at two different targets if able.
* While under the effects of Blood Greed, prefers two Hewing Greataxe attacks for increased damage.
* Uses Slaughterer’s Call before combat to rally minotaurs and gain tactical advantage.

#### Doombull
* Begins combat by charging to knock a target prone.
* Follows up with Barbed Fist to inflict wounds that can be exploited by fellow minotaurs.
* Coordinates attacks to keep the target prone, maximizing damage with Hewing Greataxe.
* Prioritizes reapplying wounds to maintain tactical advantage if the target recovers.

\columnbreak



##### Minotaur Adventures

 | d8  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Unholy Portal:** A group of minotaurs is guarding a mysterious portal in the forest, believed to be a gateway to a dark realm through which demons emerge. The players must fight their way to the portal and find a way to close it to prevent further incursions.|
|  2  |**The Crumbling Lair:** The players are tasked with exploring ancient ruins that have recently become overrun by minotaurs. The ruins are believed to contain powerful artifacts and lost knowledge. The minotaurs, led by a brutal warbull, are using the ruins as a base for their raids. The players must clear out the minotaurs and uncover the secrets hidden within the ruins. |
|  3  | **The Labyrinth's Heart:** An ancient maze-like structure, rumored to be the sacred ground of the beastmen, has been discovered deep underground. The players are tasked with exploring this unholy labyrinth and reaching its heart, where a warbull is said to guard a forbidden secret. |
|  4  | **The Hunting Grounds:** The players are hunted by a group of elite flesh gorger minotaurs known for their relentless pursuit of prey. They must use their wits and survival skills to turn the tables on their hunters, leading to a final confrontation with the minotaur leader in their own hunting grounds.  |
|  5  |**The Butchers’ Massacre:** The players come across a village decimated by a group of minotaurs known as the Butchers. Corpses are strung up as gruesome warnings, and the surviving villagers are in desperate need of help. The players must hunt down the Butchers, stop their reign of terror, and find a way to ensure the safety of other nearby settlements. |
|  6  | **Siege of the Sacred Grove:** A grove considered holy by a local druidic circle is under siege by minotaurs led by a doombull, who aims to desecrate the site and devour its inhabitants. The players are enlisted to break the siege, protect the druids, and drive back the beastmen. |
|  7  | **Relic of Doom:** A powerful relic capable of enhancing magical abilities has fallen into the hands of a minotaur transforming it into a doombul. The players must venture into beastmen territory to retrieve the relic before the doombull can fully harness its power to lead a devastating attack on nearby human settlements.  |
|  8  |**Fresh Meat:** A doombull known as The Butcher dwells in labyrinthian catacombs under a desecrated cathedral, and his insatiable appetite has claimed numerous adventurers and travelers. The players are hired to seek him out and put an end to his slaughter.  |

### Minotaur Loot
Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from minotaurs are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying, though it is common to harvest horns from their fallen. Most dropped valuables can be found using an **Intelligence (Investigation)** check.

Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.


#### Minotaur Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

##### Minotaur Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 3 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-5  | 2d4(5) 5sp Items |
|  6-10 | 2d6(7) 5sp Items | 
|  11-17 | 2d4(5) 1gp Items  |  
|  18-21 | 2d4(5) 2gp Items |  
|  23+ |  2d6(7) 2gp Items |
